The Daily News reported that the United Association of Anti-Japanese National Salvation Societies of Various Universities convened its seventeenth executive committee meeting at 4:00 PM on the 20th. All executive members were present, and sixteen important matters were resolved. Item three was kept confidential at the request of the standing committee and therefore could not be announced. Additionally, the association issued two telegrams this morning to the Provincial Party Headquarters, the Provincial Government, and the Wujin County Party Headquarters regarding the punishment of traitorous merchants in Wujin who were undermining the anti-Japanese movement. These telegrams are recorded below.

(Resolution) Handed over to the Propaganda Department for responsible handling (6) This association should establish a fixed meeting procedure (Resolution) Handed over to the General Affairs Section for handling (7) This association's office staff should have badges (Resolution) Handed over to the General Affairs Section for handling (8) This association should report the student union members and contact addresses to all members (Resolution) Handed over to the Documentation Section for handling (9) Should this association provide assistance regarding the traitorous merchants in Shanghai, Shantou, and Changzhou who are undermining the anti-Japanese movement? (Resolution) Shantou and Changzhou should telegraph the provincial government, requesting strict punishment of the traitorous merchants and troublemakers, and telegraph each local Anti-Japanese National Salvation organization to work diligently. Alumni Association of Japanese Universities and Higher Schools

Planning for Anti-Japanese National Salvation Methods

The Shanghai Alumni Association of Japanese Universities and Higher Schools recently convened a meeting of all members to plan for anti-Japanese national salvation methods. It was learned that the association had recently convened another general meeting and two executive committee meetings, as well as one general affairs group meeting. The important matters resolved in these meetings are as follows: (1) Association members will swear an oath of eternal non-cooperation with Japan, as follows: "I solemnly swear, with utmost sincerity, never to cooperate with the tyrannical Japanese, and to do everything in my power to seek anti-Japanese national salvation. So help me God." (2) Zhou Changshou, Ma Zongrong, Zheng Zhenwen, Yin Rugeng, Wang Zhaorong, Zi Yaohua, Zhang Menglin and others were elected as executive committee members. (3) A Japanese Goods Investigation Department was established, with Zi Yaohua and Yang Junsheng appointed as directors, to connect with external organizations investigating Japanese goods. In addition to investigating Japanese goods, they will also investigate substitute goods. (4) An Anti-Japanese Goods Self-Sufficiency Planning Committee was organized, first focusing on the research of Japanese goods and working in coordination with the Shanghai Alumni Association of Workers and Students in Japan, dividing the research into nineteen sub-groups according to research items. (5) Suggesting to various universities that they establish Japanese Research Societies, in order to thoroughly and universally understand Japan's national power and national conditions. (6) Contacting the Alumni Associations of Universities and Higher Schools in Tokyo to inform fellow alumni that they can contact this association when returning to China, so that the anti-Japanese organization can increase its strength. (7) All alumni of universities and higher schools serving in Japanese institutions or organizations must withdraw without exception, taking unconventional methods to resist the Japanese and show determination. These plans are currently being actively implemented.

Education Sector Drafting Anti-Japanese National Salvation Education Construction Plan

Resolutions of the Municipal Teachers' Anti-Japanese Association

The Shanghai Municipal Teachers' Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association held its second executive committee meeting yesterday at 2:00 PM in the conference room of the Municipal Party Headquarters. More than twenty people attended, including Hu Shuhua, Huang Zao, Cheng Kuanzhi, Wang Wujun, Wang Xiaoying, Zhou Darong, Zhang Zaibo, Chen Jicheng, Tang Tonghou, Shen Tianbai, Tao Baichuan, Ma Jiazhen, Wu Xiu, Dai Yuxian, Lu Xinfu, Zhou Feicheng, and Tong Xingbai. Huang Zaoxiong chaired the meeting, and Cheng Kuanzhi recorded the minutes. The following important matters were resolved: (1) Hu Shuhua, Yi Xingbai, Wang Xiaoying, Shen Tianbai, Zhao Lüqing, and Zhou Darong were appointed to draft an Anti-Japanese National Salvation Education Construction Plan to be submitted to superior authorities for adoption and implementation. The draft must be completed before the next meeting. (2) In response to the arrival of Guangdong peace representatives in Shanghai, Hu Shuhua, Huang Zaoxiong, Zhou Feicheng, Wang Xiaoying, Zhao Lüqing, Chen Jicheng, and Dai Yuxian were appointed as seven committee members to act as representatives to extend their regards and to seek guidance on anti-Japanese national salvation policies.

Inaugural Meeting of the West District Private Elementary School Teachers and Staff Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association

Yesterday at 4:00 PM, teachers and staff of private elementary schools in the West District held an inaugural meeting at the Global Student Association. A total of more than 50 representatives from the district attended. The Shanghai Municipal Private Elementary School Teachers and Staff Anti-Japanese National Salvation General Association sent a representative, Cheng Ming, to chair the meeting. Feng Shuhua, a representative from Qinghua Middle and Elementary School, recorded the minutes. The chairman first reported the purpose of the meeting, and then representatives from Peiming Affiliated Elementary School, Global Affiliated Elementary School, Qinghua Middle School Affiliated Elementary School, Aiwu Elementary School, and Tongshan Elementary School were elected as district executive committee members. Furthermore, representatives from Qinghua Affiliated Elementary School, Peiming Affiliated Elementary School, and Global Elementary School were elected to attend the General Association. Numerous practical anti-Japanese national salvation plans were discussed and resolved, and telegrams were sent to the League of Nations, urging them to uphold justice, and to the National Government, urging them to quickly establish a foreign policy. It was also decided to convene the second membership meeting next Saturday at 2:00 PM.

Two-Jiang Women's Physical Education First Aid Team Swearing-in Ceremony

Performing Various Nursing Techniques...Organization Divided into Twenty-Four Teams

Yesterday, the Two-Jiang Women's Physical Education School First Aid Team held a swearing-in ceremony at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. Approximately 300 people attended, including Municipal Party Headquarters representative Yu Zhongbiao, Municipal Education Bureau representative Zhou Shanglai, Bin Chuminyi, Wang Xiaolai, representatives from various schools, and team members. Ms. Lu Lihua, the school principal, chaired the meeting and reported that the team was organized into 24 teams, each with five members. The American instructor stipulated that the first aid team complete 20 subjects in a short period of time, while the nursing team would be taught all methods of caring for patients, striving to complete preliminary studies as soon as possible. Next, after speeches by the Party representative and the Education Bureau representative, instructors Ms. Zhang and Ms. Yang performed various first aid and nursing techniques for an hour. Finally, the oath was taken, photos were taken, and the meeting adjourned. The oath is recorded below: "We will spare no sacrifice to fulfill our national responsibility, to provide sincere and loving first aid to the soldiers on the front lines, to abide by nursing discipline, and to promote the national salvation spirit of women. We solemnly swear."

30th Anniversary Celebration of Wuben Girls' Middle School

On October 24th, the Shanghai Municipal Wuben Girls' Middle School held its 30th anniversary celebration. Considering the current national crisis, the school authorities temporarily suspended all originally planned entertainment and exhibition events. Only a celebration ceremony and a student military review were held at the school and the public stadium from 9:00 AM that morning. Since implementing military training, the school's female students have demonstrated orderly steps and outstanding performance.

Sports

Foreign Characters

Banned on Student Sports Uniforms

The Ministry of Education, considering that it is inappropriate to overuse foreign language markings on Chinese students' sports uniforms, issued a special order to education departments and bureaus in all provinces and cities to ban this practice. The Central Executive Committee Secretariat issued Public Letter No. 2380, requesting the Zhejiang Provincial Executive Committee to submit a request to ban the overuse of foreign language markings on student sports uniforms at all levels nationwide. A copy of the original request was attached. Approval was granted, and it was determined that the overuse of foreign languages for markings on student sports uniforms at all levels should be banned. In addition to replying by letter and distributing the order, the original attached request is copied and issued to all schools under the jurisdiction of the Zhejiang Provincial Education Bureau for compliance.

Special Document: Liu Haisu's Report to the Ministry of Education After Returning to China (4)

In the spring of the 19th year, I went to Italy to conduct research. In the autumn of the same year, I went to Belgium to review the international exhibits at the World's Fair. I also discussed with authorities and art world scholars in both countries, and they all agreed to assist. In the spring of the 20th year, Haisu was invited by the Chinese Academy of the University of Frankfurt, Germany, to lecture on Chinese painting. I repeated the proposal and immediately held an exhibition of modern Chinese paintings at the Frankfurt Art Museum. In June, it was moved to Heidelberg for exhibition. The immense impact at the time was beyond expectation. This was because in the early spring of that year, the Japanese had held a large-scale exhibition in Berlin, where the works were mostly manufactured to cater to the psychology of Europeans. As a result, Europeans felt that Eastern art was merely imitating the superficial aspects of Europeanization without showing its unique strengths. Upon seeing the exhibition of modern Chinese paintings, they were surprised and impressed. The art was simple and natural, without artificiality, which was incomparable to the Japanese's laborious efforts to create falsehoods. The embassy also felt that it was necessary to hold an exhibition of modern Chinese paintings in Berlin after seeing the German press coverage. Therefore, they telegraphed Haisu, urging him to go to Berlin. I formally negotiated with the Prussian Academy of Arts, the Oriental Art Society, and other institutions, and repeatedly discussed with Oriental scholars, Professor Kuemmel of the University of Berlin, Professor Amersdörfer, Vice President of the Academy of Art, Professor Parschmen of the Department of Engineering, and others in detail. Finally, the embassy formally signed an agreement with the Oriental Art Society to hold the exhibition in February 1934, with the Prussian Academy of Art as the exhibition venue. Ten German committee members and one representative from the German Ministry of Foreign Affairs were recommended.

President of the German Oriental Art Association, former German Ambassador to Japan, Solf

Vice President of the German Oriental Art Association, Doctor of Engineering, Klemperer

Secretary General of the German Oriental Art Association, Director of the Oriental Museum, Professor Kuemmel of the University of Berlin

Deputy Secretary General of the German Oriental Art Association, Director of the National Museum, Cohn

Professor of the Berlin University of Technology, Government Building Consultant, Boerschmann

Director of the National Art Library, Professor Glaser of the University of Berlin

Chief Accountant of the German Oriental Art Association, Dr. Ginsberg

Deputy Chief Accountant of the German Oriental Art Association, Count vonareHeydt

Secretary General of the Prussian Academy of Art, Professor Amersdörfer of the University of Berlin

China first recommended the Minister and Vice Minister of Education, the Director of the Central Research Institute, the Minister to Germany, and Haisu as committee members to carry out preparations. The remaining six people will be added later.

The process of these negotiations was fraught with difficulties. With the basic outline in place and a path vaguely formed, Haisu returned to his homeland to appeal to the government and to the people of the country, hoping that everyone would work together to make it a success, and not allow the Japanese to usurp the role of the master of the East. This is what Haisu has hoped for day and night.

Humble Suggestions Regarding Chinese Art Facilities

Since Haisu's travels in Europe, I have seen the grand scale and profound significance of the art facilities in various countries, and I have been deeply impressed and unable to contain myself. Looking at my homeland, I feel sad and heartbroken. This is because China has thousands of years of rich artistic heritage that far surpasses Europe. However, due to the lack of proper preservation and development methods, it has been buried and neglected. As a result, later scholars cannot fully appreciate the achievements of previous generations, nor can they pursue in-depth creation in modern times. Instead, others have stepped in to take over, collecting remnants overseas, indulging in ancient times, and lamenting that Egypt and Greece have no successors. The pain of this situation is even greater. Now that the country is focusing on economic construction, it is not too late to remedy the situation. I offer my humble suggestions for selection and hope to work together with the people of the country to reverse the decline of art and elevate national culture to modern standards. This would be a great blessing.

Free Talk

The Sound of Anti-Japanese Resistance

— Zizai

The tyrannical Japanese are wreaking havoc, and the entire country is indignant. Many schools are training volunteer soldiers to prepare for the worst. Shooting practice is extremely important. My family originally had two large air rifles. They were often used for practice. Recently, my two sons were both assigned to the volunteer army at school. Every morning at home, they draw a red sun in the center of a white piece of paper in the courtyard as the target for shooting, symbolizing that every bullet is aimed at the Japanese flag. When volunteer armies practice shooting targets in various places, it is best to also draw a red sun as the target, to indicate the purpose of the shooting.

Not Removing the Weeds in the Courtyard, Zhai Fu's Miscellaneous Talks

Reading Lenin's Biography

Fulep Müller's "Lenin and Gandhi" has the following passage regarding Lenin's education policy:

"…His education was intended to prevent people from exceeding the knowledge and education permitted by the government of the day. In this way, the people in the proletarian state would not be stirred by too much knowledge and the danger of reflection. Lenin, on the one hand, attacked illiteracy, and on the other hand, suppressed free science…" Lenin was unwilling to allow the people freedom to seek knowledge. Only air and knowledge should be unrestricted by people. After reading this passage, I could not help but protest. I wrote a few lines of indignation at the time, and now I will publish them:

"The people's ignorance cannot be used, loudly awakening the deaf; fearing difficulty in controlling them when enlightened, suddenly wanting to shut their ears. Like a country relative, wanting to send gifts and also being jealous."

Guangbing is a Supplement for Soldiers

— Yang

Almost everyone has eaten Guangbing sold in the market, but few people know why this cake is named "Guang." In these days of anti-Japanese fervor, it is especially important to study it. It will surely invigorate your spirit. Originally, Guangbing was made by Qi Jiguang, a Ming Dynasty general. General Qi's name was Guang, so the cake was named Guangbing. Qi Jiguang was a great man in China's history of resisting Japanese pirates. In those days, the coastal areas of our country suffered from the poison of Japanese pirates. The misery was no less than the current situation in the three northeastern provinces. At that time, the government troops also dared not resist. Fortunately, this respectable and lovable Qi Jiguang was born, winning much glory and achieving many military exploits for our country. After he sent troops, he beat the Japanese pirates into a rout, fleeing at the sight of him. There was absolutely no word "non-resistance" in his mind. He treated the Japanese pirates like killing pigs. He was strict, brave, and admirable in his military actions. At that time, the Japanese were so afraid of the name of General Qi that even children dared not cry. He was only concerned that the soldiers would be hungry after prolonged battles, reducing their strength to kill the enemy. He specially came up with this convenient Guangbing. Each soldier could carry it with him. It was also easy to eat. When the soldiers were happy to fight, they could eat while killing. Eating and killing at the same time, killing them all. Once, a large group of Japanese pirates even killed up to Beiling, forty miles away from the provincial capital of Fuzhou. The situation was extremely critical. Duke Qi commanded his troops to resist, ordering his son to be the vanguard. He ordered the soldiers not to look back. Those who violated the order would be beheaded. After the army left the east gate, his son turned back to see if his father had left the city gate. Duke Qi saw it and immediately ordered him to be beheaded. Therefore, his soldiers bravely charged forward, each one worth ten men. After winning the victory, when they returned to the place where his son was killed, he thought of his son and built a pavilion on the spot, called the Son-Thinking Pavilion. It still exists today. Everyone, think about whether this Duke Qi is worthy of being a Chinese soldier. When you eat Guangbing, you should think of Duke Qi and learn from his loyalty and bravery. Quickly take back the three northeastern provinces and become today's Duke Qi.

World Small Chronicle

— Haike

Canada's War Memorial. Canada has recently built a national war memorial. It is expected to be completed by the end of this year. It costs about 50,000 pounds. All the work is undertaken by a British family. This family can be called an artistic family because six brothers and one sister in the family can all work on it. It has been working since 1926, which shows the scale of the project.

Spanish Love Work. There is a province in Spain called Barcelona, which can be said to be a free land. In one place that is not free, if women fall in love with men, they cannot act alone. They can only talk about love in front of a female guardian. It is impossible to make intimate and sweet expressions. Even kissing must wait until after the engagement before it can be implemented. Young people generally think it is a great suffering.

Politicians and Detective Novels Detective novels are intriguing and interesting, and can develop the mind. Therefore, many people around the world love to read them. The great modern British politician and former Prime Minister Lloyd George and S. Baldwin are both avid readers of detective novels. In their spare time, they use detective novels to relax.

Twenty-Four Hours of Reflections

— Yang Jifu

Last year, I made a brief tour of the Northeast in early spring. Everything I saw and heard was heartbreaking. Entering the customs, I visited Nankai University in Tianjin and met Mr. Zhang Boling (at that time, Mr. Zhang had just returned from Japan after the failure of the Chinese delegation to the Far Eastern Games). Mr. Zhang asked: "You came from Liaodong. What are your thoughts?" I said: "I certainly have thoughts, but I feel that I don't know where to start. What I saw on this trip was that the economy of the Northeast was completely under the control of the Japanese. The Japanese no longer need to add political and military aggression. Like the furniture in the house and the gold and silver treasures in the boxes and chests, everything has been taken by them. What is the need for sweeping? The political affairs of the Northeast are exactly like this. If the Japanese want to annex and seize it, it is tantamount to asking for trouble. However, the destruction of the Northeast will only take twenty-four hours." Mr. Zhang said angrily: "It is not just the Northeast that is like this. China can be destroyed in twenty-four hours. Open your eyes and see if there is any defense at the ports of the country. Now Japan has occupied the Northeast in twenty-four hours. Alas, my words have unfortunately come true. I only hope that Mr. Zhang's words will be fortunate enough not to come true." (Transferring Donations to Relief)

Prophetic Sounds

— Red Ice Child

Prophecies are sayings. Honorable people do not esteem them, but how can those who perished be at peace? The one who revives the Han is named 'Show'. When Tu is high, the Cao Wei dynasty will flourish. A quick pill signals the demise of the Manchu Qing. Nursery rhymes and folk sayings unintentionally come true after the event. Is this not what Zhuangzi meant when he said, "The Dao is in the urine and excrement"? Here are four examples selected and recorded on the left.

Eastern carriages and horses are commonly seen and ridden by people on the roads. Now, they recklessly incite conflict and seek trouble for no reason. They take advantage of our natural disasters and add troops to our borders. They are utterly barbaric and without principle. Is it not the East wrong? (Homophone) Could it be China that is wrong?

"Doing a thousand, doing ten thousand, but not doing a business that loses money" is a common saying in the business world. To resist the uncivilized and unreasonable Japanese barbarians, boycott enemy goods, and sever economic ties is the supreme strategy for national survival. "Don't do business with Japan" (Homophone). Our merchants have long foreseen this.

"There is sky, but no sun," is also a folk saying. In essence, the old name of Liaoning and Shenyang was Fengtian. If we want to recover the Fengtian homeland, we must prevent the Japanese from rising to prominence. Only then can our territory be complete and intact.

Mr. Liu Haisu's Reflections on His European Art Study Tour (Part 2)

— Ji Ping

"Spiritual Resonance and Lifelike Dynamism" is a very difficult concept to explain, yet it is extremely important. These four characters can be broken down and explained one by one from "Spiritual Resonance," "Resonance," "Lifelike," and "Dynamism." They can also be sharply divided into two segments and explained separately from "Spiritual Resonance" and "Lifelike Dynamism." Alternatively, "Spiritual Resonance and Lifelike Dynamism" can be interpreted as a single noun.

"Spiritual Resonance and Lifelike Dynamism" has recently become a single, indivisible term in the Chinese art world. At most, people say it contains "lifelike dynamism with spiritual resonance" or "lifelike dynamism permeated with spiritual resonance." In reality, lifelike dynamism in the universe is invariably permeated with spiritual resonance. Spiritual resonance is bound to be expressed through lifelike dynamism. If we were to replace it with a foreign term, as in the aforementioned five methods, we could readily use the word "Rhythm." The English critic Walter Pater said in his famous work "The Renaissance," "All art constantly aspires towards the condition of music." Therefore, rhythm is not only the state of music but also a state inherent in all art. Understanding this point will make it easier to comprehend the significance of spiritual resonance and lifelike dynamism. As I mentioned above, spiritual resonance and lifelike dynamism are, on the one hand, the ultimate completion of Chinese painting creation, and on the other hand, the highest criterion for criticism. Xie He meant exactly this in the past. In the first aspect, creation can achieve spiritual resonance and lifelike dynamism because it has the primary condition of "brushwork." What has been discussed above is very clear. In fact, it can also achieve spiritual resonance and lifelike dynamism, for example, "the subtlety of distinct styles is also entering the realm of divine." However, writing without losing brushwork is the best. This has also been discussed above. As for structure and imitation, they also rely on brushwork to highlight their characteristics. Then brushwork is very important and mysterious in Chinese painting. Yes, Xie He also regarded brushwork as innate, saying, "Heavenly talent and innate knowledge cannot be attained through learning." At the very least, there must be "overflowing intention and novel brushstrokes." We can regard the overflowing intention as the arrival of inspiration. The painter's creation is not like a machine that runs every day. He can only put pen to paper when he has the inspiration to inspire, at least when he is content and joyful, or even when he finds joy in sorrow. He described Gu Junzhi's creative situation as follows: "He once built a multi-story building as a place for painting. He would not pick up a brush during windy, rainy, or hot weather. Only on days when the weather was mild and the air was refreshing would he take up a brush, ascend to the building, and remove the ladder. His wife and children rarely saw him." Gu Junzhi was like this. There must also be someone who does the opposite and starts writing in windy, rainy, or hot weather. Therefore, the achievement of spiritual resonance and lifelike dynamism in creation is actually mostly a component of genius.

"Old days don't make good dramas" This proverb means that vulgar people should not be associated with for long. Using the enslaved Koreans to cruelly massacre overseas Chinese is a trick that is not a good drama. A good drama, the audience shouts with praise. It is pitiful that the Koreans are only doing puppet show, really a puppet play. I know, in the world stage, this play is destined to not win applause.

A letter from Mr. Shou Juan states that at a Ningbo fellow-villagers association gathering, the two ladies Yu and Tang initiated a painting exhibition for flood victims from various provinces. There, he saw a painting "Autumn Scenery on a Balance" by Mr. Chen Xiaodie, signed "Dieye." The excellent coloring and imagery made it unforgettable. Regrettably, paintings were purchased by ticket number, preventing arbitrary selection. He does not know whose hands this pearl has fallen into. I deeply admire this painting and wish to purchase it at a high price. I wonder if you, sir, could disclose this information. If the owner is willing to part with it, please send a letter to the "Freedom Talk" section of your newspaper, entrusted to Mr. Shou Juan for delivery. I would be immensely grateful. With best wishes, respectfully, Tuian. Shou Juan's note: My friend Xiaodie's paintings are elegant and free. Those signed "Dieye" are his carefully crafted works. He cherishes his reputation and will not part with even one painting for any amount of money. Even in ordinary exhibitions, his works are rarely seen. Recently, he has made a grand vow for the flood victims in various provinces. He is collaborating with Qian Shoutie on Buddhist images, each priced at thirty yuan, with a quota of one hundred pieces, all proceeds donated to relief efforts. I heard that more than half have already been purchased. However, I also deeply admire Dieye's landscapes. After more than ten years of close friendship, I only obtained a "Violet An Diagram." Since Dieye has made a grand vow, I hope that in addition to Buddhist images, he will create several landscapes for a solo exhibition, with all the proceeds donated to relief. Wouldn't that be an even greater act of merit? Anyone who agrees with my words, I am willing to take the lead in initiating this, and I ask Tuian what he thinks.

Department Wheel Assembly

The Pestle of Dreams (20)

— Cheng Zhanlu

Mr. Tao Chi advocated armed peace. After hearing these songs, he no longer insisted on his usual views. He leaned against a tree, nodding his head, tapping his toes, appreciating and murmuring to himself...

"That's right, in this era of great justice, China will not be subjugated. People are born to seek happiness, not to seek troubles for themselves. I am truly prone to excessive worry." "Tao, friend, are you here!" A singing girl greeted him from afar.

"Here! Come, come, come!" Many singing girls echoed the greeting.

"Coming! Coming!" Tao Chi could not help but step forward to meet them.

"May I ask your name, ladies?"

"We sing in the modern paradise, and we are all called modern singing girls."

"May I ask how old you are, ladies?"

"My age is sixteen, her age is also sixteen, and all their ages are sixteen. Moreover, this year is sixteen, and next year will also be sixteen, and the year after that will always be sixteen."

Tao Chi listened to these words, seeming to understand yet not understanding. He left the singing girls and continued forward, vaguely walking into a restaurant. Inside, many young men and women were holding a modern dinner party and invited Tao Chi to join them, simply because there was an empty seat at the party.

"May I ask, gentlemen, what is the occasion for this dinner party today?"

"Mr. Tao, we do not use the word 'today.' With today, there is the past yesterday and the future tomorrow. We have none of those here, only the enduring present."

"Is this place perpetual daylight?"

"We only live forever under the all-encompassing morning light, with no end or night... With day and night,"

"We cannot maintain our present. We are overthrowing day and night."

Among them, the most popular was the unified tax, accounting for more than 2.5 million, and the 20% tariff was about 2 million yuan. Although there was no new development in the diplomatic situation, the domestic peace and reunification problem was very optimistic. The bond market environment was generally very good, but the silver money industry was tight, and large investors did not have huge investments. The popularity of buyers was rarely improved. The market was still dominated by zero households and arbitrage. Therefore, although the market prices of various bonds were generally higher than the previous day, the trend was very stable. The old short households were not willing to make up for the settlement, and they were ready to deliver goods at the end of the month. The long side was in danger of being squeezed by those who could not receive the goods. Therefore, although the buyers had a slight advantage, the overall situation of supply and demand was very balanced. The front and back markets were always trapped in a hovering state, and the stagnant situation was unseen for several weeks. As a result, the futures for the next month, such as the 20% tariff, rose by more than 1 yuan, and other multi-good rose by several corners, but the establishment of the whole 6 continued to fall slightly, and the spot for the 20% tariff fell quite a lot compared with the beginning of the week.

Continued Progress in the Cotton Market

American cotton has shown a tendency towards weakness, but gold prices are slightly stronger, and two major firms have purchased a particularly large amount of bales, approximately over 20,000 dan (a unit of weight), resulting in almost all available cotton being bought up and a tighter market atmosphere. However, actual cotton transactions in the market remain non-existent, with no inquiries being made, due to prices being too high while foreign cotton remains cheaper. Forward contract factories are still selling, and the future trend will continue to depend on the direction of American cotton.

Hankou futures continue to rise. The opening price of Hankou standard cotton futures was affected by the falling trend of American cotton, causing scattered small investors to become soft and hesitant. The Situation in the Grain and Riverine Rice Market is Slightly Stronger

Nantou: Yesterday's rice market saw few sources from the western routes. Transactions in the city were more active than before, and it was rumored that Zhabei was increasing purchases. Various shops took advantage of this opportunity to buy more inventory. New japonica polished rice of two grades saw prices increase by 12 jiao (a unit of currency). The Bai Ge Yao variety was still selling sporadically. The Ningbo variety was somewhat popular in the local market, with prices rising by 1 jiao. Transactions for fresh and aged Lu Yang Tip rice were sluggish, and the market remained flat. Fluctuations in the exchange rate were limited. Water chestnut tips have already dropped to zero.

Xinzha: Yesterday's arrivals were about 20-30 boats. Due to the sharp drop in prices in the previous few days, traders suffered losses. The prices in the inland areas initially followed the downward trend in the Shanghai market, but inquiries from buyers turned firm. Morning trading was excellent, with fresh and aged goods from Changzhou and Wuxi being the most popular, with prices rising by a few jiao. The Nanbang varieties, including medium-red rice and white rice, sold well. The market saw no rise or fall. The glutinous rice market was slightly tight. The Budu Tip variety was affected by foreign rice and showed a downward trend. New Kunshan japonica rice arrived briskly, but sales were sluggish with prices down 2-3 jiao.

Foreign Rice Trading is Quiet

Yesterday's foreign rice market saw no movement from the North gangs and a wait-and-see attitude from the local gangs. Overall trading was quiet, and the market gradually returned to a state of calm. Although foreign rice trading companies were selling, there were no inquiries from buyers. Moreover, the October shipments sold last month and at the end of September have already arrived in port one after another. Therefore, everyone's sentiment is bearish. Although the buyer gangs have an appetite, they are mostly waiting and seeing, waiting for prices to fall before taking action. The overall market only saw a small transaction of 100 bags by a local gang for a small profit of 10.04 yuan per bag.

Futures Market is Generally Flat

Yesterday's flour market saw a generally flat trend after the opening in the morning, with various market participants having their own positions. Because of the mixed influences of foreign wheat, the prices for various months' positions were stable with a slightly bullish undertone. By the afternoon opening, near-term positions remained stable due to tight money conditions, while long-term positions saw a sharp rise. Rumors that the contracted foreign wheat was involved in an accident at an American port, and that European countries such as France had also ordered 30-40 million bushels from the United States, led to predictions that the price of foreign wheat would soar. Therefore, market sentiment was excited, and prices peaked step by step. It remains to be seen whether there will be further positive developments. As a result, the current month rose by 7.5 li (a unit of currency), November to January rose by 2.5 fen (a unit of currency), February rose by 2.25 fen, and March rose by 2.75 fen.

Wheat Futures Jump Sharply in the Aftermarket

Yesterday's wheat futures market saw stable prices in the morning opening, with little increase, only 2 fen different from the previous day. However, at the afternoon opening, both near- and long-term contracts saw a sharp rise, and trading was unusually active. This was due to rumors that the contracted American wheat had been involved in an accident, and that France had ordered a large quantity of American wheat. By extrapolation, the source of foreign wheat was expected to be restricted, causing dormant market sentiment to suddenly rise sharply. The difference between the high and low prices compared to the previous day reached 1-2 qian, and if this rumor is confirmed, there may be another wave of excitement. As a result, the current month rose by 8 fen compared to the previous day, November rose by 1 qian, December rose by 9 fen, and January to March each rose by 1.2 qian.

Silk and Tea Factories Continue to See No Improvement in European Sales

Yesterday, the silk market in Shanghai remained unchanged. Reports from Lyon indicated that sales of Shanghai white filature silk were not improving and that French sales were still stagnating. Although American firms were negotiating for spot and futures, their bids were still demanding, and various manufacturers found it difficult to accept due to heavy costs and small profits resulting in large losses. Yesterday, only Hexing purchased 10 bales of medium-to-superior Shanghai white filature silk. Weicheng purchased 10 bales of Hubei cocoon Shanghai yellow filature silk, and Gaobei and others purchased 15 bales of coarse yellow silk. Prices remained flat and weak.

Jili Raw Silk Continues to be Shipped to Shanghai

Over 200 Pieces Transported from Xun and Zhen Ports Yesterday

Recently, sales of Jili raw silk to Europe and the United States have been sluggish, and inventories of new silk in the producing areas have increased sharply, leading to increased shipments. Yesterday, Jili raw silk continued to be shipped to Shanghai from Xun and Zhen ports, with 220 pieces of Xiu, Lin, Qing, and Ma brand silks being transported by Mei Hengyu and others. Zhen Mei Green Tea Shows Slight Movement

Yesterday, the tea market in Shanghai remained quiet. Although Jinlong, Dode, and other firms made small purchases of Zhen Mei, Gong Xi, and Zhu tea, these were only to replenish stock and not for large-scale demand. The long-stagnant Zhen Mei green tea saw the British firm Jardine Matheson issue a large number of pricing telegrams, and the market has shown slight movement. However, the proposed market prices are more than 20 taels (a unit of weight) lower than before, so it is difficult to be optimistic about the situation.

Needle and Xiu Mei Teas See Slight Movement in British Sales

Piece Goods, Sleeve Linings, Printed Cotton Fabrics Sell Well

The current woolen fabric market can be described as stable, but it is a pity that the exchange rate for shillings has increased significantly, and it is predicted that market prices next spring will be extremely chaotic. Yesterday, horsehair sleeve linings and printed cotton fabrics sold extremely well, and foreign firms were busy shipping goods. Yesterday, Tahe's wholesale price was 1.125 yuan per yard, and the retail price from shops was 1.75 yuan.

Navy Blue Melton Sells Well and Rebounds

Melton cloth is currently selling well, and local buyer gangs continue to purchase it. Most of it is used for Western-style clothing and overcoats. Prices once fell due to abundant inventory and sluggish sales. Yesterday, prices rebounded, with navy blue being particularly popular, rising sharply by several fen per yard. Only navy blue and yuan-colored Melton cloth are available. Yuan-colored cloth is sold to the Sichuan gangs, and navy blue is sold to local and Zhejiang inland small buyer gangs. The Sichuan gangs completed their purchases a month ago, and the local gangs are currently slowly making purchases.

Metals

New Lead Wire Sales Reached 600-700 Dan Yesterday

Metal trading saw significantly reduced sales in the northern routes due to the war, while sales in the south were limited due to tight money conditions. Coal

Hongqi Coal Has Ample Inventory

Recent arrivals of Hongqi white coal have been strong, and inventory is ample. Surveys of various warehouses show current stocks of over 7,000 tons. Sales are not particularly active due to seasonal factors. High-quality screened lump coal is priced at 22 taels per ton, while the smaller cinders screened out sell extremely well, as demand has increased from sand-spreading, laundry work, and small factories. Therefore, prices are also very firm, currently selling at 17.5 taels per ton.

[Local News]

Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, and Others Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

Over a Thousand People Expressed Enthusiastic Welcome. Guangdong Representatives Released a Joint Statement. Cai Yuanpei Discussed that the Meeting Emphasized Diplomatic Efforts.

Cai Yuanpei, Zhang Ji, who are working for peace, along with Guangdong representatives Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, Li Wenfan, Wu Chaoshu, Chen Youren, and others (5 people in total) arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning at 10:00 am aboard the President Madison. Accompanying them were Tang Shengzhi, Zhang Fakui, Gan Jieshou, Guo Taiqi, as well as staff, clerks, and servants, totaling 91 people. Representatives from various national government agencies and civic organizations went to the dock to welcome them, with over a thousand people attending, making it a grand occasion. After disembarking, Wang and the others drove to visit Hu Hanmin, with whom they had not met for a long time, and they had a pleasant reunion. They then gathered with central committee members remaining in Shanghai to discuss everything. Chairman Jiang is scheduled to come to Shanghai in the next few days to meet. It has been decided that the peace and unification conference will be held in Nanjing, with only an exchange of ideas taking place in Shanghai. Wang and others expressed to people yesterday that party comrades should unite sincerely and have high hopes for the future of the peace conference. Here is a summary of the details of yesterday's arrival in Shanghai and the statements of the Guangdong representatives.

Shantou Encountered a Storm

The President Madison of the Da Lai Company was originally scheduled to arrive the morning before yesterday, but due to encountering a severe hurricane and dangerous waves in Shantou, it was forced to reduce its speed. Therefore, it was delayed until 8:30 am yesterday morning to enter the Wusongkou and arrived at the Bund at 10:00 am, berthing at the No. 16 and 17 floating pontoon wharves in Yangshupu, arriving 24 hours late.

Welcoming the Representatives

Yesterday, the representatives who crossed the river to board the ship to welcome the delegates included: National Government representatives He Yaozu and Shao Yuanchong, Chairman Jiang's representatives Chen Mingshu and Yang Hu, Central Committee members Li Shizeng, Wu Tiecheng, Yu Youren, Shao Lizi, Chu Minyi, Ding Chaowu, Zhou Qigang, Zhu Peide, Zheng Hongnian, Zhang Qun, Gu Mengyu, Hu Hanmin's daughter Miss Mulan, and Chu Minyi's wife, numbering dozens of people. In addition, those waiting to welcome them at the Customs House Wharf included: students from universities and middle schools in Shanghai, the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, the Shanghai Seamen's Trade Union, trade unions from various industries, the Chinese Nationalist Party Protecting the Party Comrades Association, the Nationalist Party Zhejiang Comrades Association, party headquarters from various districts in the city, the Citizens' Federation, the Shanghai Guangdong Overseas Chinese National Salvation Federation, and women's groups, numbering over a thousand people. The wharf was extremely crowded, and latecomers had no room to stand. Temporary martial law was imposed near the wharf, cutting off traffic.

Martial Law on the Bund

Yesterday, the Bund area in Yangshupu was under martial law. In addition to the Municipal Public Security Bureau dispatching a special water patrol team for strict defense, port police from the Customs House went to protect the area. In addition, the Municipal Public Security Bureau temporarily dispatched many policemen to assist. Investigators from the British and French concessions were dispatched to follow the ship to protect it. Pan Lianbi, the detective chief of the British Concession Police, Cheng Ziqing, the director of the political department of the French Police, and others also went in person.

Photograph of Guangdong Representatives Arriving in Shanghai (Taken by This Newspaper)

Temporary Ferry Yesterday morning, the Jianghai Customs House specially prepared the Jinghui small boat, and the Public Security Bureau prepared two small boats. In addition, Chu Minyi privately borrowed two ferries from Du Yuesheng to transport the welcoming personnel across the river to board the ship to welcome the representatives.

Boarding the Ship to Welcome the Representatives

The President Madison berthed at the Bund at 10:00 am yesterday morning, and the welcoming personnel boarded the ship one after another to greet them. For a time, the deck was noisy with voices. Wang, Sun, Li, Wu, Chen, and others shook hands with the welcomers in the hall. Wang was dressed in Western-style clothes and his attitude remained the same. At 10:30 am, Wang and the others disembarked and boarded the Public Security Bureau's ferry. At 11:10 am, they landed at the Taikoo Wharf. Those waiting there held banners and cheered. Wang frequently nodded in response.

Joint Statement

The Guangzhou Extraordinary Conference sent Mr. Wang Jingwei, Mr. Sun Ke, Mr. Li Wenfan, Mr. Wu Chaoshu, Mr. Chen Youren, and others to Shanghai to discuss peaceful unification matters. Wang and the others arrived in Shanghai on the morning of the 21st aboard the President Madison. In the midst of the enthusiastic welcome from all sectors, the reporter stepped forward to ask about the purpose of this trip. The gentlemen made a brief statement, which is excerpted below: (1) The reporter asked, "What is the purpose of this trip?" They replied, "Since its establishment, the Central Extraordinary Conference has aimed internally to establish democratic politics and overthrow personal dictatorship, and externally to thoroughly defeat the aggressors of imperialism and seek China's absolute freedom and equality. However, our method of resolving the current situation differs greatly from those who purely seek victory by force. We believe that unification can only be achieved through construction, and joint governance can only be achieved through power-sharing. For months, colleagues at the Extraordinary Conference have been working hard to achieve the above goals. Unexpectedly, Japanese imperialists suddenly sent troops to forcibly occupy the three northeastern provinces, massacring countless of our compatriots, destroying countless of our properties, trampling on our sovereignty, and humiliating our nation to the utmost. Anyone with blood in their veins cannot tolerate this. This time, colleagues were ordered by the Extraordinary Conference to come to Shanghai to discuss peaceful unification, with the aim of completing our consistent advocacy, concentrating the power of the whole country, striving internally for the realization of democratic politics, and externally planning to jointly deal with the national crisis, vowing to resolve the current diplomatic difficulties in our country on the principle of not losing a single inch of our country's territory or sovereignty. Not losing power and not humiliating the country is our consistent external spirit, and it is also the basis of the Nationalist Party's glorious history in the past." (2) The reporter asked, "Can we hear about the process of promoting unification in Shanghai this time?" They replied, "The disputes within the Party and the country in recent years have been extremely painful, but they have also been unavoidable. Therefore, at the beginning of the establishment of the Extraordinary Conference, we announced to the people of the country the spirit of seeking service without competing for victory. Fortunately, the two sides have confronted each other for months and have not met in battle, which is also a great fortune in misfortune. Since the Japanese troops forcibly occupied the three northeastern provinces, Cai Jiemin

The Grand Welcome from the People (Taken by Liguang Studio)

Mr. Zhang Puquan and Mr. Chen Zhenru were ordered to go south and brought a handwritten letter from Mr. Chiang Kai-shek expressing his sincerity in seeking unification of the country and jointly dealing with the national crisis. We immediately invited the three gentlemen to Guangzhou and proposed that the Guangdong government issue a circular telegram agreeing with Chiang's resignation and the cancellation of the Guangdong government produced by the unification conference in order to establish a unified government. The three gentlemen expressed their approval and jointly drafted a telegram to be issued by Chiang, stating that he would resign after the establishment of a unified government, and to be issued by the Guangdong government, stating that the Guangdong government would cancel this decision after the establishment of a unified government. The telegram and draft were telegraphed to Chiang by Cai, Zhang, and Chen. Chiang replied that he agreed in principle, but the wording of the telegram had to be carefully revised before it could be issued, and asked the Guangdong side to send responsible comrades to Shanghai to discuss it. At the same time, we also learned that Mr. Hu Zhantang had safely arrived in Shanghai, so the Extraordinary Conference immediately passed a resolution at the 16th Congress to send colleagues and others to the north that day." (3) The reporter asked, "Do you have a pre-determined plan for resolving national affairs this time?" They replied, "Colleagues and others do not hold the idea of competing for victory, nor do we come for the purpose of dividing spoils. Therefore, even if there are pre-determined plans, they are nothing more than fundamental improvement methods concerning the party affairs, politics, military, diplomacy, finance, and other systems. The general idea has been seen in the Extraordinary Conference's circular telegram to the Maruichi on the current situation. Due to the short time, we regret that we cannot elaborate on the detailed plan."

Meeting at the Hu Residence

Wang Jingwei, Sun Ke, Wu Chaoshu, Li Wenfan, and Chen Youren, etc., disembarked at the Bund of the French Concession on the Great Horse Road at 11:00 am yesterday and took cars directly to the Hu residence on Muirhead Road to comfort Mr. Hu and discuss the grand plan for peaceful unification. Mr. Hu also kept everyone for lunch and had a pleasant conversation. Wang and Hu expressed their closeness when they met. Everyone talked straight until 1:15 pm before excusing themselves. Soon, Wang and Chen, etc., together with Sun Ke, took cars to Sun's residence at No. 10 Rue Moliere to continue the discussion. Zhang Ji, Cai Yuanpei, Chen Mingshu, Wu Tiecheng, and Li Shizeng also arrived one after another and held a tea party at the Sun residence to discuss peaceful unification. Zhang and Cai left at 3:00 pm first, and Chen and Wu also left at 4:30 pm one after another. Wang talked straight until 5:00 pm before leaving Sun's residence. There was news that the committees will hold another discussion at the Hu residence that evening. According to a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency, the discussions among the committees at the Wu residence included (1) the committees agreed to first organize a unified diplomatic committee to unify diplomatic policies in order to deal with foreign affairs first (2) The various problems regarding party affairs, politics, and the military will be considered in detail after Chairman Jiang arrives in Shanghai. It will not be announced for the time being.

Talks by Zhang and Cai

Zhang Ji and Cai Yuanpei, who came with the Guangdong representatives, told reporters from this newspaper yesterday that comrades of the party, in view of the current national crisis, have resolved to be consistent in dealing with foreign affairs. There is no form of meeting in Shanghai, and external rumors of a preparatory meeting and other things are not facts. Chairman Jiang will come to Shanghai in the next few days to meet and exchange ideas again. After both parties agree, the Guangdong representatives will go to Nanjing for formal consultations. The parties are now concerned about not internal personnel disputes, but focus on consistency in dealing with foreign problems, and so on.

Confucius Visits Wu

Minister of Industry Kong Xiangxi

Visited Guangdong representative Wu Chaoshu at his private residence at around 3:00 pm yesterday to discuss diplomatic policy for a long time. Not long after, Li Liejun, Xu Qian, Cheng Qian, and others visited Sun Ke and then went to the Wu residence to meet with Wu. Wu Tiecheng also had another meeting until around 5:00 pm before excusing himself.

Wu Chaoshu Talks

Mr. Wu Chaoshu received a reporter from this newspaper yesterday and said that in the face of the current national crisis, we must do our best to unite the strength of the whole country and deal with foreign affairs consistently. As for this peaceful unification, the Guangdong side will work hard to promote it. The unification conference is determined to be held in Nanjing. The parties will only exchange views in Shanghai. Regarding diplomatic negotiations with Japan, our country has asked the League of Nations to uphold justice, but the League of Nations does not have the strength to support it. Only economic power, and whether the countries can consistently comply, is also a problem. Therefore, it is actually difficult to prevent Japan's violence. Although the United States has

has the strength, it is very clear whether they are willing to risk sacrifice for us. Therefore, the final way is self-help. If diplomatic efforts reach the end of the road, of course, we will have to take self-defense measures. The reporter asked about the external advocates for restoring relations with Russia. What does Mr. Wu think? Wu replied that there is no problem in restoring relations with Russia. In fact, relations in the Northeast have already been restored. After restoring relations, prohibiting their propaganda is another matter, which has absolutely no impact. Even if relations are not restored, Soviet Russia's propaganda can still be carried out unhindered. Mr. Wu also released an interview with a Xin Sheng News Agency reporter yesterday (Q) How will military and political powers be divided in the future? (A) We have always advocated that military power should be under the control of the party and the government. (Q) Will the first, second, and third session committees attend the peace conference completely? (A) This is the case when discussing party-related issues. (Q) Then will the official meeting be a tripartite meeting of the party, government, and military? (A) This depends on the results of the exchange of views in Shanghai before we know.

Guangdong Telegram

Anti-Japanese Association Unifies Inspection Rights

All Circles Should Register Inspection Sections

Automatic Inspections May Be Rejected

The Shanghai Municipal Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association issued Public Notice No. 13 yesterday regarding the unification of the right to inspect Japanese goods throughout the city, stating: According to the resolution of the third Standing Committee meeting of this association, the Inspection Department of this association is the highest authority for inspecting Japanese goods throughout the city. If other circles set up special inspection sections, they may be allowed to register with the Inspection Department of this association to assist this association in handling matters. The Japanese goods seized must be reported to the Inspection Department of this association immediately for personnel to receive them. Furthermore, the fifth Executive Committee meeting resolved that the inspection of goods in stores should be handled by the association together with the inspection teams of the relevant trade associations. Currently, it is found that various circles often spontaneously conduct inspections of goods. Although the enthusiasm is commendable, the resulting malpractices can easily lead to impersonation and fraud. Loving the country is therefore misleading it. A special urgent notice is hereby issued, urging all circles to comply with the regulations. Furthermore, all companies, factories, and stores, except for trade associations, may inspect and seal the stores of their associations, but the disposal of Japanese goods should still be reported to this association for handling. In addition, regarding those who do not hold the triangular badge of this association and the staff certificate with a photo attached, all should be rejected when they come to inspect. This is of utmost importance.

This is of utmost importance.

Japanese Deliberately Provoke Trouble on Avenue Doumer

Opening Fire with a Handgun, Wounding a Policeman

At 0:15 AM this morning, a car came from North Sichuan Road at the corner of Avenue Doumer and East Yokohama Road. It passed through East Avenue Doumer and drove towards West Avenue Doumer, then turned back to the intersection of East Yokohama Road and stopped next to a small house 30 meters away from the police post. The policeman saw the chauffeur running over, shouting in a panic, "The Japanese are hitting me!" At this time, five Japanese chased from behind. Without asking the reason, they surrounded the policeman. Three Japanese tried to snatch the policeman's gun. After a few minutes of confrontation, one of the Japanese fired a handgun, and the bullet hit the policeman's left back of the hand, piercing through the palm. For self-defense, the policeman drew his gun and fired back, passing through the right sleeve of the Japanese's coat and grazing the palm. The assailant Japanese fled. The policeman also returned to the Public Security Bureau and reported to the Sixth Team. At that time, it happened that Fifth District Inspector Gao, Chief Inspector Chen, and patrolmen passed by and were surrounded and beaten by another group of Japanese. After investigation, the car number, 12609 in the Concession's registration, belonged to the Zhongshan Motor Company on Zha Pu Road. The chauffeur's name was Lu Peiwang, and the injured policeman's name was Wang Changshun. The assailant Japanese were Matsumoto, Nishimura, and a Taiwanese man named Gao. After the incident, Japanese Marine Corps Adjutant Yasuda led the Marine Corps in cars to the scene. On the Public Security Bureau's side, Fifth District Chief Wang and Team Leader Sun led the police to maintain order. After a while, City Government staff member Chen and the head of the Dithaisiwei Road Patrol Room arrived and negotiated with Yasuda. As a result, Yasuda ordered the Marine Corps to withdraw. A Browning pistol shell casing was found at the scene, which was obvious evidence that the Japanese had fired the gun. The head of the patrol room took it away.

Letter from the People of Jilin to American Investigators

Relating the Miserable Situation of Being Oppressed by the Japanese Army, Every Word a Tear

Since the Japanese used force to occupy Liaoning and Jilin, it has attracted the attention of various governments. The United States government specially sent the Counselor of the US Embassy in Japan, together with the US Consul General in Harbin, to South Manchuria to investigate and find out the truth. When the two arrived in Jilin, some respected people in Jilin jointly sent a letter to the two investigators, detailing the actions of the Japanese army after occupying Jilin, asking them to pay attention. Now a friend from Jilin has copied and sent the letter to Shanghai, asking for it to be published. Therefore, it is translated and published below. Reading it will further reveal the general atrocities of the Japanese in the eastern provinces. The general idea of the original letter is as follows: "(Titles omitted) We are pleased to know that Your Excellencies have come to Jilin to investigate with the good intention of maintaining international peace. We express our welcome. We assume that Your Excellencies urgently desire to obtain accurate information regarding the current real situation here. Therefore, we dare to state the following facts for reference: (1) The reorganized Chairman of the Jilin Provincial Government, Xi Qia, is under the strict surveillance of the commander of the Japanese army stationed in Jilin. Two Japanese military police guard his side day and night. All his words and actions are completely devoid of freedom, and he must obey the orders of the Japanese army commander in everything. Therefore, all political and financial affairs in Jilin Province are now actually under the control of the Japanese army. (2) On September 25, the Jilin Provincial Government held a reorganization under the threat of Japanese bayonets. Everything was directed by the Japanese army. Before the reorganization, two Japanese soldiers sent by the Japanese consulate pointed guns at Xi Qia, making him unable to resist, and this lasted for more than an hour. (3) All police in the provincial capital are completely under Japanese command. (4) All actions of the Japanese army are carried out at night in order to avoid public attention. (5) The following places are where the Japanese army is stationed: (1) the Provincial Government, (2) Dong Daying, (3) the Military Training School (translated name), (4) the headquarters of the 34th Regiment. In addition, the Japanese military police have also set up a command post at Erdao Wharf (translated name). (6) Since June 3, the Japanese army has been building a military airfield four or five li from Gaogang Road Station, and digging trenches near the station. (7) All railway stations, telegraph offices, radio telegraph offices, etc. in Jilin are managed by the Japanese army, and they inspect local newspapers, mail, and all official documents of the provincial government. (8) Pedestrians passing through Xinkai Gate after 7:00 PM are all subject to Japanese inspection. (9) The Japanese army arbitrarily searches without reason. There have been incidents of robbery of women's gold jewelry in Chinese residences from Jichang Railway Station to Xinkai Gate. (10) The Japanese army frequently breaks into schools to search students and teachers. If they find books containing the Three People's Principles, they will arrest them. (11) On September 22, the Japanese army arrested Han, the chief of the military law department of the Jilin provincial government. His whereabouts are still unknown. It is said that he has been killed by the Japanese army. (12) Japanese expatriates residing in Jilin are issued firearms by the Japanese army and have become armed plainclothes soldiers. (13) Since Jilin City was occupied by the Japanese army on July 21, the residents have been extremely frightened. Most of the students have fled, the schools have been suspended, and everything is in a state of emergency. The above is about the current situation in Jilin. As for the actions of the Japanese army after occupying Jilin, the following points should be noted: (1) The Japanese army's occupation of Jilin is not to protect Japanese expatriates but to invade Chinese territory. This can be proved by the above-mentioned facts and the following two points: (A) Since September 18, when the Japanese army occupied Shenyang, the Jilin Provincial Government has repeatedly declared to the Japanese consulate that it is willing to do its best to protect Japanese expatriates in the province, and there has never been any danger to the lives and property of Japanese expatriates since then. (B) When the Japanese army entered the city, it did not focus on protecting Japanese expatriates but hurriedly occupied official offices, provincial banks, and other banks, as well as telegraph offices and radio telegraph offices, and sent troops to guard the city gates. (2) We, the people of Jilin, express our firm opposition to the Japanese army's occupation of our territory. (3) The entire Jilin province is under the military rule of the Japanese army. Although the Japanese claim to the world that they have withdrawn their troops, the Japanese army invading Jilin has not actually withdrawn. If the Japanese army does not withdraw for a day, Jilin province will be under Japanese control, and the people of Jilin will not be able to get rid of fear and pain for a day. We deeply hope that Your Excellencies will pay attention to these facts, etc." (Omission below)

Phoenix Matches Prove to be Japanese Goods

The Shanghai Municipal Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association replied to the letter from the Smoke and Exchange Industry Association yesterday, stating: After this department consulted the Investigation Department and dispatched personnel for a thorough investigation, we have now received a reply stating, in brief, that although Phoenix brand matches are sold by Ruizhong Foreign Firm, we do not know its origins, which led us to believe that it was a Swedish product. But in fact, the Phoenix brand sold by Ruizhong Foreign Firm is in cooperation with the Japanese Datong Phosphorus Company. In terms of share capital, the Swedish merchant accounts for 51%, and the Japanese merchant accounts for 49%. Under such circumstances, the Phoenix brand cannot be regarded as a Swedish product. Moreover, the matches produced by the Huesheng Company in Shanghai are completely Japanese goods, and the brands used are all Chinese goods. Therefore, Phoenix brand matches should be confirmed as Japanese goods without any doubt, etc. Accordingly, we hereby reply for your information, hoping that you will instruct your colleagues to refuse to use them.

Municipal Finance Bureau Announces Direct Revenue Figures for September

More Than 160,000 Yuan More Than the Same Month Last Year The Municipal Finance Bureau announced yesterday that the total direct revenue of various donations and taxes in September of this year was 455,767 yuan, one jiao and three fen, which was an increase of 169,196 yuan and two fen compared to the same month last year. Among them, the revenue from housing donations was 261,084 yuan, two jiao and six fen, an increase of 109,350 yuan, six jiao and eight fen compared to the same month last year. The revenue from business tax was 61,157 yuan, nine jiao and four fen, an increase of 32,026 yuan, three jiao and eight fen compared to the same month last year. The revenue from slaughter tax, vehicle donation, boat donation, etc., also increased.
