Local News Two

Pacific Conference Inaugurated

131 Representatives from Nine Nations Attend

Discussing Pacific Commercial Relations

Shen Shi Telegraph Agency reports: The Pacific International Studies Conference commenced yesterday (the 21st) morning at the International Recreation Club on Bubbling Well Road. Participants included 131 representatives from nine countries: China, Austria, the United Kingdom, Canada, Japan, New Zealand, Fiji, the United States, and the Netherlands, along with 45 secretaries from various national delegations. At around 9:00 AM, a round table meeting began, discussing "Pacific Commercial Relations." Discussions were divided into four groups, chaired by: Group 1 – Mr. Copetto; Group 2 – Mr. Ding Wenjiang; Group 3 – Mr. Ross; Group 4 – Mr. Shu Wang-Mai. A recess was taken at 10:45 AM, followed by a joint session of all four groups at 11:15 AM. At 12:30 PM, the Chinese Committee hosted a banquet for all committee members. Chairman Xu Xinliu delivered a welcoming address, followed by a speech by Mr. Green, President of the Pacific Association from the United States. Representatives from various countries read congratulatory telegrams and messages from their respective governments. President Chiang Kai-shek's congratulatory telegram was read by Mr. Chen Liting. Finally, Dr. Hu Shi, the conference president, delivered a speech, fluent and moving, touching the entire assembly. After the banquet, a group photo was taken, and the meeting adjourned. From 8:30 PM to 9:45 PM in the evening, Dr. Ding Wenjiang and three other notable figures lectured on economic development, geology, and other topics. The discussion proceedings and welcoming speeches are recorded separately below.

Chinese Committee Members in Each Group

The round table meetings yesterday were divided into four groups for discussion. The Chinese committee members in each group were as follows: Group 1: Wu Daquan, Xu Shuxi, Pan Guangdan, Ms. Zeng Baosun, He Lian; Group 2: Xia Jinlin, Chen Liting, Ning Encheng; Group 3: Hu Shi, Liu Jingshan, Madam Liu Zhanen, Dong Xian Guang, Ms. Wang Guoxiu, Ms. Wu Yifang; Group 4: Xu Xinliu, Zhang Boling, Tao Menghe, Zhang Zhuping, Yan Yuhang.

Discussion on Tariffs and Silver Prices

The four round table meetings discussing Pacific commercial relations primarily focused on the two issues of tariffs and silver prices, but other related events were also briefly mentioned. (1) Regarding the tariff issue, it was generally agreed that announcing a tariff moratorium or a period of tariff stability would be appropriate. However, realizing this would inevitably encounter many difficulties, with the issue of dumping being a particularly challenging point. Although all countries recognize their unwillingness to engage in dumping in other countries, there is no universally recognized definition of "dumping," and there are no accurate reports on the extent of dumping. Therefore, one of the suggestions put forward to the research committee is to undertake research on this point. The public also generally recognizes that increasing tariffs would increase the burden on consumers and hinder the development of international trade. However, economic nationalism often tends towards increasing tariffs. Although Japan adopts a protectionist tariff policy, it is heard that domestic opinions are quite divided, and doubts about the suitability of this policy are gradually increasing. For example, Japan uses a protectionist tariff policy to develop its national chemical industry, but there are also arguments in favor of allowing Germany to produce various chemicals, while Japan focuses on producing other goods that can be sold to Germany in exchange. However, the opposite is true in China. Generally, economists who theoretically believe in free trade advocate that China should currently adopt a protectionist tariff policy. Their reasons are firstly, China is in a world of protectionist tariffs, and secondly, China's industries are mostly in their infancy, so temporarily implementing protectionist tariffs is a justified measure. (2) The general conclusion regarding silver prices is that the decline in silver prices is not the cause of China's economic downturn, but rather the economic downturn is the reason for the decline in silver prices. As for the rise in silver prices, opinions on whether it is beneficial or detrimental to Chinese commerce are quite divided.

The various round table meetings made several practical suggestions to the Order and Research Committee, one of which has been unanimously agreed upon: the importance of improving Pacific commercial statistics. It was also suggested that the research department of the conference investigate. Other suggestions included studying the development of eliminating domestic and international economic barriers and abstractly researching whether the abolition of Pacific tariffs would be appropriate. When conducting this problem, if we can first study what practical impacts hypothetical free trade will have on various industries, we will be able to take more intelligent actions. Also, because expert opinions on these events differ greatly from national policies, it is advocated to study whether educational institutions can be used to train public opinion and reduce their separation.

Xu Xinliu's Welcoming Address

I have the opportunity to extend my sincere welcome to the representatives of the Pacific International Studies Conference for the third time. Although there may be an end to my welcoming words, my enthusiasm for welcoming them will increase day by day. Although there have been many changes during the preparation period for our gathering here to celebrate the opening of the conference, we are still very happy to be able to gather together today. Moreover, various tools of peace are now in danger of being broken one by one, but the Pacific International Studies Conference alone can stand still and resist all destructive forces. This is what we should be proud of. Today, in addition to representing the Chinese Council for the third time to express its sincere welcome to all of you, there is little else I can say. I am confident that we can fully meet the expectations of the general public for the Pacific International Studies Conference. Our attendance at this conference reflects our firm belief in the value of the Pacific International Studies Conference's steady and unbiased thinking. Please rise and join me in a toast to the realization of the ideals of the Pacific International Studies Conference and the success of this conference.

Hu Shi's Speech

Distinguished guests, this fourth Pacific International Studies Conference, although slightly different in form, has faced many serious doubts in the past few weeks. The Chinese representatives, as hosts of the conference, suddenly encountered a major national crisis, the severity of which has never been seen in history. Moreover, with this conference being held in China, although there is no formal public war between China and Japan, these two major countries on both sides of the Pacific are indeed in a state of war. The entire Chinese nation is being ignited by a strong sense of shame and resentment. At the beginning of their emotional upswing, the Chinese representatives could not help but doubt the usefulness of peaceful and deliberative international tools like this Pacific International Studies Conference. You probably already know that the Chinese Council proposed several times the possibility of postponing the conference, and the Japanese delegation also wanted to cancel the conference.

In the days before the conference, it seemed that this fourth Pacific International Studies Conference would be postponed. Looking back now, all the doubts, disappointments, and emotional outbursts have been completely dispelled and fully forgiven. We are always human, so we can't escape all kinds of weaknesses. This major international situation suddenly added to us is to test the degree of our faith in a doctrine, but we are not prepared. This crisis is too strong for those of us with weak faith. Now I dare say that all the Chinese representatives want to deeply apologize to all the representatives because in this unfortunate period, all these difficulties have caused you great inconvenience.

But today we are gathered together to hold the fourth Pacific International Studies Conference. Looking at the conference venue, the ceremony, and the slightly reduced number of representatives, this conference has changed somewhat, but as I said, this is a major conference. Allow me to take this opportunity to say a few words.

This conference has succeeded in the midst of fragmentation, thanks to the patience, wisdom, philosophy, and political talent of the general members of the conference, especially the philosopher chairman. Are the methods and ideals of this Pacific International Studies Conference only applicable to times of world peace and goodwill among all countries?

Today's meeting is not only forever memorable and a memorable page in the history of the Pacific International Studies Conference, but it is also worthy of commemoration in terms of the nature of international relations, agencies, and organizations, because it has established a glorious precedent. Many people can boast of having international minds in times of peace, but when reason is unreasonable and emotions are agitated, they calm down, study patiently, and discuss impartially.

But gentlemen, we should not be complacent because of this success. This international conference is still in its infancy. We have many thorny issues waiting for us to analyze and solve. If we observe these issues with an erroneous attitude and deal with them with prejudiced eyes, then our spirit and the methods we use will inevitably fail. If our views of others are obscured by emotions and prejudices, we will also fail. If we go astray, dye ourselves with the colors of sophistry for a particular belief, or have the spirit of a confessing sinner for a particular case, we will always fail.

On the first day of our work here, we must have a clear understanding of the nature of our problems and work. These problems are problems of countries and nations. Our work is for these countries and nations. For a nation or for many nations, this is the most sacred trust, but it is also the most dangerous work. This work, in the words of Chinese sages, "one word can make a country prosper, and one word can destroy a country." We can only remove prejudices to bear this sacred responsibility and resolutely prevent our thoughts and judgments from being obscured by prejudices and emotions. We are not here to cry, nor are we here to laugh, but only to understand everything. We are not here to teach, but only to exchange opinions with each other. As long as we have a harmonious spirit to seek the truth, then if there is a small success, it can be achieved.

Mr. Green's Speech

In brief, on behalf of the Pacific Council and all members of the conference, I would like to express our sincere gratitude for the welcome we have received. Preparing for such a conference is not an easy task. It requires many people to spend their time, energy, and goodwill to achieve it. The fact that we can generously meet this need shows not only the sincerity of the Chinese people's hospitality, but also the greatest purpose of the Pacific International Studies Conference, namely, to promote international friendship in the Pacific to obtain mutual sympathy and understanding, which is a direct service and has the highest value. Such gatherings allow men and women of insight from countries along the Pacific to conduct open investigations and patient research. No matter what issues are discussed, its success can be predicted. The conference's formal agenda promotes orderly thinking on urgent and important issues, and the knowledge thus increased will surely be of great value. What we have gained is first, to observe problems from the perspective of others. Although differences of opinion and conflicts of interest may still exist after the discussion is over, if we can maintain our opposition with a sincere, frank, and humble attitude, we will be able to respect each other and change the atmosphere. Second, cooperative research. The help obtained in various controversial issues enables today's civilized countries to abandon war and use peaceful meeting methods. People's psychology often follows the path of relying on laws and not valuing private fights. National psychology, which is progressing, may not be like this. This kind of change cannot be achieved overnight. Habits are derived from repeated experiences. However, its trend is already evident. Since the conclusion of the Treaty of Paris, the signatory countries have had a solemn obligation to promote it. Although there may be doubts about whether the League of Nations can be an effective mechanism for international cooperation, if all countries, whether they have joined or not, have the hope of peace and support it with all their strength, it will be able to make it a successful and effective tool for the people of the world and completely abandon the use of war as a tool of national policy. The Pacific International Studies Conference is also in the process of testing this same purpose. People who are skeptical and critical cannot be avoided, but we can all ignore them here. We only need to move forward according to the established route, engage in discussions and research unswervingly, and do not use investigation tools for propaganda. Judging from the experience of the past six years, the value of meetings and research has been demonstrated, and politicians from various countries are also paying close attention to the achievements of this conference. The greatest purpose of this conference is to enhance the mutual relations between countries, so we are not afraid to discuss even the most serious controversial issues. Many disputes are due to cultural reasons. If we can contact each other and exchange ideas and break down the barriers of language and writing, we can prevent the occurrence of international conflicts.

We hope that your visit to China and believe that your discussions at the conference will make an important contribution to promoting international relations in the Pacific. I am convinced that the ideals of world peace and international friendship will never be realized unless men and women from all countries, such as those attending this conference, are willing to spend their time and energy to study and understand the complex problems between countries. Today, the international community is filled with clouds of ignorance and malice, so we must do our best to maintain and consolidate the peacekeeping mechanisms that have been painstakingly built since the establishment of the League of Nations and the Kellogg-Briand Pact. In this atmosphere of suspicion and misunderstanding, the Pacific International Studies Conference is undoubtedly sufficient to fill this much-needed position and promote scientific knowledge and arouse rational sympathy among thoughtful people in various countries. The Pacific International Studies Conference will be able to establish its foundation for a more hopeful future.

News of Disaster Relief for Flood Victims

Huayang Yizhen Association's Disaster Relief Work

Qingjiang Area

The association received a telegram from the Qingjiang branch yesterday, stating that the flood situation in the Qingjiang area is most severe along Hongze Lake. It is planned to distribute flour in Siyang County. Investigations have already begun on the 19th and distribution will be implemented immediately.

Funing Area

A letter from the Yancheng branch stated that the organization of the Funing branch has already begun. Emergency relief has already been distributed in various places, but the most important thing at present is to find ways to help the victims in the aftermath. Most of the victims will return home. Returning home is not difficult, but there is no way to solve the problems of clothing, food, and shelter. Not only is starvation inevitable, but the houses of the victims have mostly collapsed and the walls have fallen. The thatched roofs have been blown away by the wind and are no longer habitable. With winter approaching, repairs must be carried out quickly. How to settle the repair costs is a matter of concern for the general association.

Taizhou Area

The Taizhou branch is organized by 33 local gentry, with the county magistrate as chairman. Most of the school buildings have been allocated for sheltering disaster victims. Every day, the lives of four to five hundred people must be maintained. It is estimated that the disaster relief work will last for more than eight months. At present, in addition to providing food for the victims, the branch's work also includes diagnosing and treating diseases, burying the dead, and so on. They are also trying to enable these victims to return to their fields and resume their work. Hetaixian and Dongtai are in urgent need of 20,000 to 30,000 yuan, because there are many places that have not been able to start relief efforts due to lack of funds.

Dongtai Area

The Dongtai shelter was opened in the last ten days of last month. The branch negotiated with the Dongtai County Magistrate and various disaster relief organizations to carry out work in the areas most severely affected by the floods. If the victims in various places do not receive adequate relief, then in winter, thousands and thousands of victims will starve to death.

Wuhu Area

The Wuhu branch has been established and the first allocation of 10,000 yuan has been remitted. The disaster relief plan has also been decided and will be implemented immediately.

Anqing Area

A temporary disaster relief association has been organized in the area to temporarily carry out work for the association. The association has decided to allocate 5,000 yuan for standby use.

Flood Relief Calligraphy and Painting Vouchers

The association received a letter from the China Calligraphy and Painting Preservation Association Flood Relief Calligraphy and Painting Assistance Association, stating that they have collected 600 pieces of calligraphy and painting, divided into numbers, and issued 400 substitute price vouchers, each paper costing three yuan. The number of pieces obtained for each number is unequal, all of which are works by contemporary celebrities and are of great value. They are now sending 100 vouchers from No. 1 to No. 100, asking them to be distributed and the money collected. After receiving the money, the association will issue a receipt and send the money to Zhendong as soon as possible. Lovers of calligraphy and painting are requested to come to the association to purchase vouchers. They can not only obtain works by famous artists, but also benefit the victims of the disaster. It is truly a win-win situation.

Zhu Qinglan's Letter of Thanks to the Ningbo Emergency Relief Association

Zhu Qinglan, Standing Committee member of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee, replied to the Ningbo Emergency Relief Association's Letter to the Provincial Flood Relief Committees, saying: I am writing to inform you that I have received the Zhan Tai letter, and have also raised 1,855.64 yuan for the Hubei flood disaster, 22 shares of Ningbo-Shaoxing Steamboat stock, and 400 yuan in whole sixth public bonds, all of which have been received. Your association's concern for the hungry and the drowning, and its extensive relief efforts are deeply admired. In addition to transferring the current funds to the disaster area, all stock and bond certificates have been entrusted to Mr. Wu Zhihao to be sold for cash. Once they are sold, the water bill receipt will be sent for verification. First, I would like to reply with thanks.

The Conclusion of the Inheritance Lawsuit of Li Hongzhang's Great-Granddaughter

Settling the Property Division Problem with Financial Compensation

Ending the Divorce Problem by Terminating the Lawsuit

Li Jia Zheng, the great-granddaughter of the late Qing Dynasty Prime Minister Li Hongzhang, the daughter of Li Fei Yun, and the niece of Li Mugong, left home on January 17 of this year due to abuse by her husband, Zhang Jinjiang. Afterwards, she commissioned lawyer Ge Zhaoji to file a complaint with the First Special District Court, first requesting her legal mother to return the dowry of 12,000 yuan and the 600 yuan savings deposit that her late father had promised to give her in his will. Afterwards, she filed another lawsuit against her husband for abuse, requesting a divorce. At the same time, Zhang Jinjiang requested cohabitation. Li Jia Zheng also filed a complaint with the First Special District Court, requesting her uncle Li Mugong and her brother Li Jiaxi to divide one-quarter of the jointly owned property left by her late father, because she was a weak and lonely girl and had difficulties in living alone outside. The court accepted all of the above matters one by one. The part of the claim for the return of the dowry has already been judged in the first instance, ordering Li's legal mother to return the full amount. The defendant did not accept the verdict and is still appealing. The divorce part is also still in the trial period. The property division part has also been preliminarily sealed by the court after the jointly owned houses on Xin Chongqing Road Xianyi Lane and other places were attached, pending trial and legal judgment. It is now known that the lawyers on both sides of the case have embraced the principles of settling matters in Ningbo, morality, peace, and have tried their best to mediate. They have obtained the consent of both parties to sign a settlement today to resolve a dispute and declare it to be calmed down. The contents are described separately below.

Dowry and Property Division Issues

The dowry was ordered to be fully returned in the first instance. The defendant, Li Zhao, did not accept the original verdict and appealed to the Second High Court Branch. After two court sessions, Chief Judge Hu repeatedly persuaded them to reach a peaceful settlement. The lawyers of both parties, based on the court's intentions, jointly mediated the property division issue. After several twists and turns, the following conditions were set: Li Jia Zheng completely abandoned the issues of returning the dowry and dividing the property. Li Mugong, Li Jiaxi, and others gave a whole number (the amount has been discussed and is approaching). After both parties signed, they requested the court to reach a settlement and withdraw the lawsuit in court. Li Jia Zheng's life will be self-sufficient from now on and has nothing to do with her family. As for whether she will divorce or remarry her husband in the future, or go to school, her family will not ask about it. However, the relationship between Li Jia Zheng and her uncle and brother has been damaged to some extent by this lawsuit. Before the relationship is restored, if they meet, both parties will still respect the elders and love the young. This treaty will be signed and implemented today.

Cohabitation and Divorce Issues

Since Li Jia Zheng filed for divorce from her husband, there have been several court sessions, but no judgment has been made so far. Yesterday was the date for the retrial. Lawyer Ge Zhaoji filed a petition with the court to request the termination of the lawsuit. The petition said: It is hereby stated that this case is scheduled to be heard again on October 21. However, due to the marital dispute between the parties, they are unwilling to proceed with it. According to Article 231 of the Civil Procedure Law, the parties may agree to terminate the appeal procedure. The aforementioned agreement shall be presented to the court hearing the case in writing or in a fixed term by both parties. Article 233 states that the parties who terminate the litigation procedure shall not continue the litigation within two months from the date of presentation of the termination. If the parties do not continue the litigation within six months from the date of presentation of the termination, it shall be deemed to be the same as withdrawing their lawsuit or appeal. It is observed that both parties in this case are willing to follow the circumstances of these two articles. Therefore, we jointly agree to file a statement, saying that we have heard that Li Jia Zheng will strive for a peaceful resolution of her marriage after the property division case is concluded.

Xue Zhaoshu, director of the Jiangnan Embankment Engineering Office, was sued by the Baoshan All-Circles Embankment Protection Committee to the provincial office for failing to effectively repair the Songbei Seawall during the typhoon a few days ago. Director Shen of the Construction Department personally went to Baoshan to inspect and submitted a resignation from the provincial government. Wife of Cheng Yun Bursts into Tears Before Speaking

Having Fully Tasted the Flavors of Marriage

Both Parties Agree to Divorce

The interpreter of Japanese lawyer Okamoto, a Chinese man named Cheng Yun, resides in the city. He married Ms. Xu Shihua several years ago. Recently, they suddenly became estranged, with Cheng frequently scolding and assaulting her. Xu, being an old-fashioned woman with no education, only knows the ancient teachings such as "Do not disobey your husband," "Serve your husband well," and "A husband is one to be looked up to for life." She accepted adversity with docility, but Cheng still did not understand her. In July, he even injured her in an assault. Xu then went to the city court to request a medical examination and took her son, Cheng Tai, to live with her mother. She hired a lawyer to file a petition with the First Special District Court, requesting mediation to allow her to live separately from Cheng. Cheng, on the other hand, first petitioned for mediation to cohabitate. After the mediation court summoned both parties and repeatedly advised them, it ultimately failed. Cheng then formally filed a lawsuit against Xu, demanding cohabitation. Yesterday morning, Judge Li Mo summoned them for trial. First, the plaintiff, Cheng Yun, stated his reasons for demanding the defendant to cohabitate. Then, defendant Xu Shihua was questioned. Before Ms. Xu could even speak, tears were streaming down her face, and she sobbed uncontrollably. She then recounted, amidst tears and sobs, the repeated abuse she had suffered from the plaintiff, and how she had served her parents-in-law and diligently cared for her husband. She said that the doctor had advised the plaintiff not to eat nourishing foods, but she would feed him a bowl of her own milk every day. Yet, he still showed no affection or righteousness to this extent. If she were to continue to live with him, she would surely be abused to death. As she had fully tasted the flavors of marriage, she now wished to spend her days relying on needlework and had no intention of remarrying. Judge Li then questioned Cheng Yun about the alleged abuse, but Cheng firmly denied any abuse, saying that if the defendant were to cohabitate with him, their relationship might recover. However, the defendant's attitude was also very firm, resolutely refusing to cohabitate. Judge Li, seeing that one party demanded cohabitation while the other absolutely refused, realized that even if he ruled for cohabitation, it would be difficult to enforce. He then advised the plaintiff to consider carefully. At this time, the defendant also verbally changed the purpose of her complaint, advocating for divorce. She volunteered to return her son, Cheng Tai, to the plaintiff and requested that the plaintiff return her clothing to her. The plaintiff immediately agreed. Judge Li then made a record of the settlement, generally allowing the two parties to divorce. The child, Cheng Tai, would be raised by the plaintiff. The defendant's clothing, stored at the plaintiff's residence, would be returned to the defendant, and the case would be closed. All transfer procedures would be handled by the old woman, Wei Panbinyuan, who had originally brought the two parties together years ago, within one week. The woman would take the child back to the Cheng family and retrieve Ms. Xu's clothing, so that the two parties would not meet and cause conflict. This shows the judge's painstaking efforts.

A Suzhou woman named Lu Xiuzhen, 24 years old, a dance hostess, was walking near Yunnan Road and Guizhou Road around 7 PM last night. She was hit to the ground by truck number 3772, severely injuring her left leg. She was taken to Renji Hospital for treatment by the police.

Hongqiao Road Repairs Completed

Route 4 Bus to Reopen on the 1st of Next Month

Hongqiao Road in Western Shanghai was built by foreigners beyond their concession. It has fallen into disrepair over the years. This spring, the British Works Bureau proposed to repair the road. However, the city government, concerned about issues of sovereignty, was reluctant to allow it. After repeated consultations, the city government finally understood and allowed them to repair the original road surface, but forbade them from expanding or widening it. Now, the entire road has been repaired, and all the bridges have been rebuilt. The Shanghai South Public Route 4 bus, which runs on this road, is scheduled to resume service as usual on the 1st of next month.

The Union of Celluloid Manufacturers in This City

Celluloid manufacturing is a recent industry in our country. There are already several factories operating in this city. It is said that their purpose is to recover rights and resist foreign goods. Therefore, they each operate according to their specialized knowledge. Since the establishment of these factories, the quality of their manufacturing, the abundance of their production, and the prevalence of their sales have shown a trend of driving out foreign goods and replacing them. The recovery of rights has indeed been considerable. Currently, these industry colleagues, in view of the rampant behavior of violent Japan and filled with righteous indignation, are urgently uniting the industry, pooling their resources and efforts, and adhering to the spirit of unity and cooperation, in order to achieve the goal of permanent economic severance with Japan. Therefore, the establishment of a union was initiated. On the 18th of this month, the Shanghai Celluloid Manufacturing Factory, Da Zhongguo Chemical Society, Da Zhonghua Celluloid Manufacturing Factory, China Ping Pong Company, Guoguang Artificial Ivory Factory, and others gathered at Daqing Lane on Nanjing Road, discussed and determined the charter, and established the Celluloid Manufacturers' Union, named the Shanghai Celluloid Manufacturing Industry Association. It is reported that they have sent letters to various agencies for record-keeping.

Central Bank Inspection Report

105th Report

The 105th inspection report of the Central Bank's issuance reserves states that, in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, the association is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the bank's issuance of convertible notes. The 105th inspection was conducted at the bank's Issuance Bureau on October 20, 1931. The results of the inspection are announced as follows: (A) The total amount of convertible notes issued is 39,699,687 silver dollars, including 36,831,225 silver dollar notes and 2,868,462 subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of reserve funds for convertible notes is 39,699,687 silver dollars, including cash reserves of 25,778,591 silver dollars. These cash reserves include 18,200,857 silver dollars stored in the bank's issuance vault, 3,943,291 silver dollars stored in branch banks in various ports, 3,626,443 silver dollars stored in correspondent banks, and guaranteed reserves equivalent to 13,921,096 silver dollars. (B) The total amount of customs gold unit convertible notes issued is 1 million customs gold units. The total amount of reserve funds for customs gold unit convertible notes is 1 million customs gold units, including 400,000 US dollars stored in a local correspondent bank at a fixed rate of 40% of the customs gold unit. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Note Regulations, 60% is in cash reserves and 40% is in guaranteed reserves. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserves exceed 60% and the guaranteed reserves are less than 40%. The inspection results are in compliance with regulations and are hereby reported. October 20, 1931. Li Fusun, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank; Supervisors Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Tai Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, and Xu Jiqing.

The First District Party Headquarters, Fifth District Party Headquarters, and Sixth District Party Headquarters simultaneously submitted reports to the Central Government impeaching him. The Sixth District Party Headquarters yesterday submitted a further report to the Central Government. The report is transcribed below:

The Sixth District Party Headquarters Continues to Report:

Reporting on the Hou Dachun case of embezzling overseas aid donations, where new evidence reveals his guilt and attempts to destroy evidence, further exposing his insidious and evil nature. A request to the government to immediately remove him from his position, order the court to file a public prosecution, and punish him severely according to the law. The reporting association is reporting on the case of Hou Dachun's embezzlement of 500 yuan donated by the Commercial Press to aid overseas Chinese in Korea under the guise of the Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Committee. After the incident, the executive committee member of the reporting association, Feng Yixian, collected evidence and submitted it to the committee, requesting a thorough investigation. At this time of intense anti-Japanese work, after the case was reported, all sectors of Shanghai society were filled with anger and unanimously demanded severe punishment to serve as a warning. If Hou Dachun still had any conscience, he should surrender and await punishment from party discipline and the law to apologize to the people. However, knowing the seriousness of the case, he dared to return the embezzled funds and destroy the evidence, displaying his insidious and evil nature, hoping to retaliate. Suddenly, on the morning of October 20th, he secretly brought 500 yuan to Wang Yunwu, the general manager of the Commercial Press, to discuss the matter and return the full amount, retrieving the temporary receipt. His intention is self-evident. After learning of the conspiracy, the reporting association immediately sent personnel with a letter to track him down. Wang Yunwu detailed Hou Dachun's fundraising and repayment process, and immediately issued a formal reply to prove it. Looking back on the massacres of overseas Chinese in Korea, the people of the country were filled with grief and indignation. All sectors of the country rushed to donate, hoping to contribute even a small amount to help those in distress. In late July, when the overseas Chinese had no food or lodging and were crying out for help, this large sum of 500 yuan was related to the lives of several overseas Chinese. Those overseas Chinese were fortunate enough to escape the clutches of the Japanese bandits, with their lives saved from the tiger's mouth. However, they were ultimately not saved, or even became vagrants and died. Who killed them? It was Hou Dachun who embezzled the donations to aid the overseas Chinese and caused their deaths. The so-called "killing without being seen" is Hou Dachun's insidious and evil heart, which is worse than the Japanese bandits, the national enemy. He turned a deaf ear to the wails of the people and did not care about the lives of the overseas Chinese. He did not know what national law or party discipline was, losing his reason and destroying his humanity. The Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Association ended on September 24th, and Hou Dachun's crimes were reported as early as October 12th. This is a fact known to all. He still thought of deceiving the heavens and stealing the sun, covering his ears while stealing the bell. On July 23rd, he raised the funds. On July 24th, the Commercial Press recorded it in the books. Now, on October 20th, after the case was reported, he asked to return the funds. After a long period of ninety days, he still wanted to cover up the truth and destroy the evidence of the crime. Is he deceiving people or deceiving the heavens? The law has clear provisions, and the crime cannot be denied. His evil wisdom is beyond the reach of others, and his stupidity is also difficult for others to achieve. If his conspiracy is allowed to succeed and his evil plan is carried out, then what heaven is there, what national law is there, and what party discipline is there? Those who are harmed and undermined in the future will not know where to turn. Respectfully reciting the Premier's revolutionary will of "revolutionizing the heart" is to show to comrades, deeply and thoroughly. To talk about revolution without revolutionizing the heart is no different from Zhi's talking about benevolence and righteousness. One horse is enough to harm the group, and one person is enough to mislead the party. In this anti-Japanese national salvation movement, how much have the Chinese people lost? Many corrupt merchants have been punished. The reason why the masses can accept sacrifices willingly and accept punishment willingly is because of the people's patriotism and the appeal of party righteousness and party ethics. If we can rectify the party, we can gain the trust of those outside the party. One cannot correct others when one is not correct oneself. Is it better to correct oneself to enhance the party's prestige, or to rectify oneself to revitalize the party's discipline? For the sake of protecting the party and the country, for the sake of tightening the anti-Japanese national salvation work, and for the sake of deepening the people's faith, we are submitting the newly obtained ironclad evidence and photocopies, hoping that the committee will review the case and immediately remove Hou Dachun from his position and permanently expel him from the party, and order the court to file a public prosecution and severely punish him according to the law to serve as a warning and maintain party discipline. The submitting association is filled with apprehension and awaits orders. Respectfully submitted to the Executive Committee of the Central Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party, Shanghai Special Municipality Sixth District Party Headquarters, Standing Committee Member Feng Xiancheng, October 21, 1931. Attached: Photocopy of the Commercial Press's reply letter, two announcements from the Shanghai Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Association received by the Relief Association, and three supplementary video photos. Original letter of proof from the Commercial Press, "Zongyu No. 778": In response to today's letter, respectfully informed that the former Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Association raised 500 yuan in aid funds from our library, which was raised by Mr. Hou Dachun and paid on July 23. Later, Mr. Hou said that because the association was reorganized, the funds had not been used and had been returned in full this morning. Inquired and replied. Respectfully, the Executive Committee of the Sixth District Party Headquarters, Commercial Press, October 20, 1931.

The Second District Party Headquarters' Submission:

The Second District Party Headquarters submits ten charges to the City Party Headquarters. The text states that it is submitting a request for a prompt and thorough investigation to clarify the truth and maintain the party's reputation. Recently, we received a public announcement from the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, stating that Hou Dachun, a standing committee member of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, used fraudulent means to solicit donations from Mr. Wang Yunwu, the general manager of the Commercial Press, under the guise of the Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Association, while serving as the standing committee member and director of the inspection department of the former All-Circles Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Committee. Mr. Wang generously agreed to donate 500 yuan. Hou Dachun then sent Wang Yongliang, a staff member of the inspection department, to the library on July 24th to stamp and receive the money. Hou then embezzled the entire amount and put it into his private pocket. The secretariat of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association learned of this and believed that it was undermining the anti-Japanese national salvation work and related to the reputation of the entire organization, so they filed a report and submitted the evidence to the Central Government for impeachment. Now, the details of the incident and the collected evidence are listed. The reporting association was shocked and inexplicable after reading it. At this time of foreign aggression and national crisis, all citizens should do their best to devote themselves to the work of saving the country, so how can they be allowed to use the name to solicit money and enrich themselves? If the allegations in the announcement are true, then the one being accused is insane, worse than a party worm or a traitor. We should all abandon him. However, although there is a cause for the incident, what is the truth? We should ask the committee to promptly and thoroughly investigate to maintain the party's reputation. Whether or not it is appropriate, we should submit a document for consideration and implementation. Respectfully submitted to the Executive Committee of the Shanghai Special City of the Chinese Nationalist Party, the Second District Executive Committee.

Hou Dachun's Notice:

Notice to the public: Recently, Feng Yixian and others have fabricated facts and submitted false accusations to the Central Party Headquarters, and disseminated pamphlets, falsely claiming that Dachun did not report the 500 yuan he solicited from the Commercial Press during his tenure in the inspection department of the former All-Circles Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Committee, accusing him of intending to embezzle the funds. I have submitted the facts to the Party Headquarters for clarification and requested a fair investigation to clarify the truth and correct the wrong. I am deeply afraid that these rumors will confuse the public's perception, so I am presenting the facts as follows: At the beginning of the establishment of the Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Association, it was decided that each committee member would raise donations. Dachun, as one of the committee members, had the obligation to raise funds. He solicited 500 yuan from Mr. Wang Yunwu, the general manager of the Commercial Press, and reported it to the standing committee members Wang Xiaochen, Wang Yansong, Lu Jingshi, and others. At that time, the official receipt of the Overseas Aid Association had not been printed. All the work of the association required funds, so I first collected the donation and advanced it, asking the association to issue a temporary receipt first. At that time, Mr. Wang Yansong advocated that there was no need to use a temporary receipt to avoid adding procedures. Dachun, who was then the director of the inspection department, felt that the association's funds were tight and the work was difficult to carry out, so he consulted with other standing committee members and agreed to use the funds first. Dachun personally issued a temporary receipt and attached a letter stating that he would exchange it for an official receipt in the future and sent staff member Wang Yongliang to the Commercial Press to collect the funds and hand them over to the inspection department for use (as evidenced by the account books of the inspection department). It was originally planned to transfer the funds after the official receipt of the association was printed, but the chairman of the Anti-Japanese Association, Mr. Yu Zhiqing, did not stamp the official donation receipt, so it could not be used. The establishment of the Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Relief Committee could have transferred the funds to the committee, but the Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Association was unable to repay the inspection department due to financial constraints, which led to the delay. This is the process of the 500 yuan being retained by the department for use. By mid-September, the inspection department was reorganized into the detective department, and Dachun was still appointed as director. Then, on September 22, the Overseas Aid Association was reorganized into the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association because of the Japanese invasion of Dong Province. The detective department of the association took over the affairs of the former Overseas Aid Committee's detective department. The amount of funds used and the amount retained was clearly stated in the transfer file and could be easily verified. Since then, the funds have been used as advances for the detective department. Until October 19, someone came to tell me that those who did not understand Dachun had collected evidence of corruption and reported it to the Central Government. After careful examination, the so-called evidence of corruption referred to this 500 yuan. I couldn't help but laugh. The funds were indeed in the detective department. Since there was an excuse, I went to the detective department to inquire. According to the director of the department, Mr. Wang Changyuan, the funds advanced by the former inspection department were returned to the Overseas Aid Association on October 4. The donation from the Commercial Press was not missing. Dachun had already explained to the Commercial Press that this kind of donation could not be solicited by other committee members because there was no official receipt, and only the Commercial Press had donated. In the future, the funds were still intended to be returned. Now that they had been returned without any loss, they should be returned to the Commercial Press as soon as possible to fulfill the previous promise. Later, Dachun withdrew the funds from the detective department of the Anti-Japanese Association and returned them in full to the Commercial Press, which was received by Mr. Wang Yunwu. Unexpectedly, rumors arose this morning, with the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation People publishing pamphlets and Feng Yihang publishing in newspapers, saying that the former director Hou had embezzled the donation, which was shocking. The staff knew the details of the donation, so how could they allow anyone to falsely accuse Director Hou with false accusations? I am stating the facts and dare to prove that the former director Hou has absolutely no embezzlement of donations. I am also submitting the pamphlets and newspaper clippings and requesting that the committee review the case and uphold justice. (Abbreviated below).

As for Dachun's responsibilities in schools and the Party Headquarters, they are also used as tools for attack, which shows his intentions even more. I will not add to the defense. Dachun has been serving in labor unions and Party Headquarters for many years, and the distinction between public and private rights and obligations is clear. In particular, the entry and exit of funds is related to personality, and I dare not be negligent. All of this is known to the public. However, in serving public organizations, resentment is inevitable. Moreover, Dachun is straightforward by nature, hates evil like an enemy, and often offends people because of this. However, I never expected that people would repay frankness with despicable means, taking advantage of the resentment. Thinking of this, I cannot help but feel chilled. Now, I have been defamed for no reason, although the truth will eventually come to light. However, those who defame me are using all means, and I am deeply afraid of confusing the public. Therefore, I dare to state the facts as above, hoping that the people of society will understand. Hou Dachun, October 21st.

Submission from Former Employees:

Guomin News Agency reports that Chen Ji, Liu Jianqi, Luo Deming, Wang Jinwu, Hu Zongzhen, Ye Huixun, Lu Xisen, Zhao Zuoyan, Cai Liansun, Zhang Shousong, Gu Rongsheng, Zhou Zifu, and other former employees of the inspection department of the former Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Committee submitted a report to the executive committee of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association yesterday on the facts of the case. The report stated that it was reporting the details of the 500 yuan donation raised from the Commercial Press for the former Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Committee's inspection department, and proving that the former director Hou Dachun was definitely not intending to embezzle the funds, requesting that the funds be reviewed to dispel the false accusations. The former inspection department of the Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Committee began operating on July 23 of this year. At that time, it was just established, and funds were needed everywhere. The association had no funds to allocate, so the former director Hou solicited 500 yuan in aid funds from Mr. Wang Yunwu of the Commercial Press. The former inspection department borrowed the funds and stated that the funds were borrowed and would be returned to the committee after the official receipts were printed and issued. Not only did the staff know about this, but many members also knew the details. On July 24, the former inspection department sent staff member Wang Yongliang to the Commercial Press to receive the 500 yuan in full. Later, the official receipts could not be issued because some members were unwilling to stamp them. The former inspection department could not collect funds smoothly and used the funds to make advances (for example, the fact that the advances pre-paid by various district offices exceeded the amount allocated by the accounting department can be verified by comparing the dates of the receipt of funds and the dates of allocation). By the end of the inspection department on September 20, it owed more than 200 yuan in operating expenses, which was paid by the association on October 4. Because the detective department needed funds, it was transferred to the detective department for temporary emergency advances. The funds were always stored in the former inspection department, now in the detective department's general director Chen Ji's possession. Until the 20th of this month, the former director Hou requested the 500 yuan to be returned. Because there was no official receipt from the Anti-Japanese and Overseas Aid Association, and the period for collecting aid funds had ended, the 500 yuan was returned to the Commercial Press and received by Mr. Wang Yunwu. Unexpectedly, rumors arose this morning, with the Shanghai Anti-Japanese National Salvation People issuing pamphlets and Feng Yihang publishing in newspapers, saying that the former director Hou had embezzled the donation, which was shocking. The staff knew the details of the donation, so how could they allow anyone to falsely accuse Director Hou with false accusations? I am stating the facts and dare to prove that the former director Hou has absolutely no embezzlement of donations. I am also submitting the pamphlets and newspaper clippings and requesting that the funds be reviewed and that justice be upheld. (Abbreviated below).

The Minli Weekly is a publication that discusses social issues, introduces general knowledge, and publishes literary works with the richest content and the most interesting topics. It is edited by Mr. Wu Hanfang. The first issue is scheduled to be published on the 24th of this month. Many of the writers are famous figures in Shanghai, especially those who are writing anti-Japanese national salvation articles. The main articles include Wu Jingxiong's "Methods of Cultivating the People's Power," Li Denghui's "Attitude That the Chinese Should Have in the National Crisis," Xia Jinlin's "How to Solve the Northeast Problem," Zhu Xunyuan's "Research on China's Economic Severance with Japan," Wu Hanfang's "A Geographical Perspective on the Three Northeastern Provinces Occupied by the Japanese," Qu Yongzhong's "A Glimpse of the World," Qiu Xing's "The Current Situation in Taiwan Under the Iron Hoof of Japan," Shao Ying's "Talking About the Sikuquanshu," as well as the famous novelist Yao Sufeng's "The Sad Emerald Girl," the famous painter Yu Jianhua's "Sketches of Yandang Mountain," and the female poet Yu Xiuyun's "New Sun Poems," all of which are rare works. Each copy of the publication costs only seven copper coins. Pre-orders are welcome. The annual subscription is 1.40 yuan. The address of the publisher is 160 Huanlong Road, French Concession.

Chinese Typewriter and Travel Pillow Stool Sell Well

Industrialist Yu Binqi invented the Chen New-style Chinese typewriter last year. After obtaining a manufacturing patent approved by the National Government, he carefully researched and achieved great success. All parts are made entirely domestically, such as steel type and rubber rollers, which were the last to be successfully developed. The typewriter has perfect equipment and is durable, so all sectors are happy to purchase it. Recently, he also invented a travel pillow stool (i.e., a steel exquisite pillow stool), which also obtained a government patent. The pillow stool uses pure steel wire as a pillar, can withstand pressure of three hundred pounds, is electroplated, white, and beautiful. It can be used as a seat or a pillow. Those who are prone to seasickness can use it to avoid dizziness. It can be raised and lowered, and shakes naturally, remaining level. When not in use, it folds to only five inches wide, eight inches long, and half an inch thick, and can be placed in a pocket like forty copper coins. It is said that the product is now in cooperation with the China Products Trading Company established by Xu Shiying, Zhang Zilian, Zhao Shouyu, Xiang Kangyuan, and Li Weicheng at No. 141 Guizhou Road, and that place has been designated as the general distributor. The company fully promotes domestic goods and welcomes all sectors to investigate and visit during this boycott period, it is said.

Notice to Readers and Correspondents

This column of readers' correspondence has always been limited to three types of questions: education, career, and marriage. Since the outbreak of the Japanese invasion of Northeast China, we have received dozens of letters every day discussing how to solve the Northeast problem and how to deal with Japan's atrocities. This is a passionate manifestation of compatriots' patriotism, which we greatly admire. Now, we would like to make an agreement with you: since you have temporarily set aside personal issues such as education, career, and marriage and are eager to study methods of saving the country, please express your opinions on the following questions:

(1) What kind of position should our country take regarding the League of Nations that would be most appropriate?

(2) What is an effective way to boycott Japanese goods? (You may focus on one industry or one region.)

(3) How can the training of volunteer armies be promoted and sustained?

(4) How can the hearts of the whole nation be united to fight against foreign aggression?

Each answer should be limited to a maximum of one thousand words. Please avoid empty talk and focus on practical methods. This newspaper will select the best submissions based on the capacity of this column and publish them for open discussion. If you agree with the methods proposed by others, please also state so. Please also provide your full name, gender, age, occupation or place of study, and native place, and attach a correspondence stamp and a sufficient number of postage stamps so that those whose letters are not published can be informed by mail. Matters concerning education, career, and marriage will continue to be handled as before. Respectfully,

Correspondence Stamp

Affix this stamp when corresponding, along with a sufficient number of postage stamps.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Yangtze River basin and coastal areas would be sunny and cold. Winds were quite strong over the Yellow Sea and East China Sea, ranging from northwest to northeast. Winds were strong in the Taiwan Strait. West of Guam, another hurricane was heading northwest-west. Its center was located within 120 miles of the intersection of 11 degrees north latitude and 140 degrees east longitude at around 6:00 AM. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 72.0 degrees and the lowest was 50.7 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 71.9 and the lowest was 48.3.

Letter to the Editor

To the esteemed Editor:

Regarding the matter of Feng Yixian exposing Hou Dachun, which your newspaper published yesterday, if any of it involves me, Wang Yongliang, I am deeply concerned that various sectors may misunderstand. I am issuing a special statement as attached, hoping it will be published. Sincerely, Wang Yongliang, October 21, with attached statement.

"Wang Yongliang's Statement"

(1) Regarding the matter of me, Wang Yongliang, signing for the payment form from the Commercial Press for Feng, because Mr. Hou Dachun and I were colleagues, and he was busy, he gave me a receipt and a letter to Mr. Wang Yunwu, asking me to collect it from the Commercial Press on his behalf. At the Commercial Press, the person collecting the payment must also sign. I was only acting as a proxy to collect the payment and hand it over to Mr. Hou of the Inspection Department. As for other circumstances, I believe Mr. Hou will make a statement. I not only did not know about it, but was completely unrelated.

Regarding the fact of receiving living expense slips, after investigation, there were nine staff members in the Inspection Department, including Wang Yongliang, Zhang Yaoming, and Sang Yutang. All staff members issued this kind of slip when receiving living expenses, which has nothing to do with this case.

Youth Garden Moves House

Min Yin

Since hearing the news of Japanese warships opening up to the Wusongkou, the atmosphere along Baoshan Road has become tense. The clouds in the sky have also become dim, and people's hearts seem to be filled with a sense of sorrow. This feeling has gradually erupted. Aside from eating and sleeping, no one is willing to do their usual work, because this sorrow has gripped the minds of a large number of people.

Yes, under such a serious and tense atmosphere, everyone is concerned about the future of the country. Everyone knows that the Northeast problem can affect the future of the entire nation.

The autumn wind has risen. This year's autumn wind is indeed not as peaceful as usual. This rustling autumn wind seems to be encouraging the development of sentimental moods. The fluctuations of nature naturally increase people's worries. The people along Baoshan Road are close to the Japanese naval headquarters in North Sichuan Road, so they naturally feel uneasy.

Xu studies at the law school. His home is in the middle section of Baoshan Road, near the western part of Baoxing Road. He used to live a peaceful reading life every day, taking the bus to school in the morning and returning from school by bus in the evening.

"Xu's life is indeed very pleasant," Xu's classmates usually said.

"That is indeed a very peaceful life, Xu's life," Xu's relatives usually said.

Indeed, Xu's usual life is most suitable for the four words "pleasant" and "peaceful." No one would issue opposing arguments to resist the criticisms of his classmates and relatives.

Now, living on Baoshan Road and attending school, Xu feels it is inappropriate to accept the four words "peaceful life" given to him. He is living a very melancholy school life.

Every day when he steps onto the bus to school, he feels an abnormal sense of boredom. He goes through school life feeling bored. He feels that living in a school environment is too individualistic. He thinks about the compatriots in the Liaoning area who are being killed by artillery shells, too many, too tragically. When he sees the newspaper, he cannot help but cry, complaining that he is a weakling, an irresponsible citizen, and a most boring citizen. He feels that such a comfortable life is not suitable in China.

The atmosphere along Baoshan Road is indeed becoming increasingly tense. From the reports of friends living nearby, he initially believed that the Japanese navy would launch a violent attack on China. Seeing the hurried situation of people hiring rickshaws to move, he felt grief. He told his parents that he wanted to move to the French Concession to hide, and at the same time, he restored his individualistic will. He liked the wealthy environment of his family. He smiled, pondered, and became excited. He forgot that he was a student, bearing the responsibility of "serving the country," bearing the responsibility of adding glory to the future of the nation. He forgot the blood of the compatriots in Liaoning, forgot the suffering fate of the compatriots. He liked to look forward to the comfortable life of moving to the French Concession tomorrow.

However, his weak attitude soon changed. He went out for a walk and found that many compatriots were working hard to resist. He felt that these many compatriots were willing to sacrifice everything to fight the Japanese to the death. The atmosphere along Baoshan Road was serious. No one wanted to move, no one wanted to live a life far away from individualism, enjoying a momentary happy life peacefully and pleasantly.

Seeing such an active and struggling atmosphere, Xu became as excited as if he had drunk coffee. His individualistic will disappeared like a cloud, his weak dreams also disappeared, and his irresponsible dreams also disappeared. He felt that the fantasy half an hour ago was truly the most shameful fantasy, the most despicable fantasy, the most boring fantasy, which should not have existed at this time of national crisis. Otherwise, this reasoning would mean that he was willing to be a "slave of a conquered nation," willing to be a prisoner, willing to be meat under the knives of the Japanese. He thought about the spirit of Yue Fei's painful drinking of Huanglong, he thought about the spirit of Goujian's sleeping on brushwood and tasting gall, he thought about many great patriotic souls of ancient times. He seemed to see their portraits in front of his eyes, glaring at him, despising him, suppressing him, warning him...

Now, Xu is moved by the idols of the great souls in his mind. He kicks up patriotic enthusiasm, he kicks up active will. Since waking up from the dream, he deeply believes that the demise of our nation is due to the lack of spirit of the youth. He deeply believes that the hot blood of dying for the country has an imperishable value. He deeply believes that this hot blood is a bright hope. He deeply believes that this hot blood is the greatest commemoration, a commemoration that adds glory to the nation. If the world does not perish, this hot blood will continue to exist, grow, and emit a tragic music.

Xu thought of these positive thoughts, and forgot everything.

"Move what house?" he thought.

"I am determined to die here, like the patriotic compatriots in this area," he continued to think.

"Dying for the country is eternal life," he stood up and shouted.

Page 21

Book and Newspaper Introduction: Two Booklets of Different Natures 丨New Era Oriental Review 丨

In this era of decline for large magazines and stagnation for small newspapers, the emergence of small booklets can truly be described as springing up like bamboo shoots after rain, becoming popular for a time. However, among these many publications, it is truly rare to find a few that are somewhat worthy of a look.

It cannot be said that there are absolutely none. For example, what I am about to introduce to the reader at this moment are a few that are relatively interesting.

1. "New Era" This publication, judging by its publication date and issue number, is still a newborn child. However, its content is the opposite, full of the demeanor of an adult, just like a young person in puberty, full of fervent emotions and lively atmosphere. Not to mention anything else, just its few illustrations, which are full of youthful enthusiasm, are enough to look down on all other booklets without shame. Now, because I do not have a current copy on hand, I cannot extract one or two paragraphs of text to introduce to the reader, but we only need to observe its material selection to know that its content is as enthusiastic as a torch. Its material selection is roughly divided into the following types:

I. Commentary In this column, we can probably glimpse the thoughts and purposes of young people in the current era.

II. Thoughts and Essays In this column, we can discover many things that the general public wants to say but dares not say, or has never said, or even things that the general public has not yet felt.

III. School News and Youth Activities This is the most important column for this publication. Any news about any aspect of various schools, as well as the activities of young people, the darlings of the era, are all available and listed in a colorful and diverse manner before us.

In short, in here, it is all what I call "enthusiasm and vitality."

According to the nature of this booklet, it is entirely a pure youth publication. Everything that young people need from various publications, it fully provides to you. Ah, this is the only good youth publication!

2. "Oriental Review" This publication is still in the initial stage, but its expression of spirit is no less than that of "New Era." If you don't believe me, please take a look at a few articles in its second issue, such as "Compatriots Arise Quickly to Save the National Crisis," "Alas, the Great Han Nation of Deities and Nobles," "My View on Japan's Dispatch of Troops to the Northeast," "Miscellaneous Talks on Northeast Border Affairs," "The Current Economic Situation of Japan," etc. From this, it can be seen that its nature is completely different from the two publications above. It is entirely a timely publication that focuses on current affairs, politics, and economics. In particular, what deserves a special introduction from me is a few of the illustrations, whose meaning is profound and powerful, admirable and unprecedented. Even compared with the illustrations in several famous major newspapers at present, I am afraid that they only surpass them, with nothing falling short.

In conclusion, I responsibly declare to the readers again that the three booklets I am introducing now are guaranteed to satisfy you after reading them, and you will definitely not say that I am deceiving you. I also add that I could have copied a glimpse of the contents of the above three publications here as proof of what I have boasted above, but in the end, due to the limited and valuable space of this column, I was unable to make such a detailed and practical introduction, which I regret very much. However, they each have their own value of existence, enough to gain your trust, so I believe that this kind of copying work is also unnecessary, so I resolutely omitted it.
